Responsive Design&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p style=&quot;text-align: justify;&quot;&gt;Parallax One is completely responsive in order to provide an optimal viewing experience, easy-reading and navigation with a minimum of resizing, panning and scrolling across a wide range of devices. Every element has been tested to ensure layout adaptability by using fluid, proportion-based grids, flexible images to build your activities future proof.&lt;/p&gt;

The images are displayed dynamically in a list sliding horizontally from one representation to the next one using subtle animations based on lightweight technologies&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;hr /&gt;
&lt;h2 style=&quot;text-align:center&quot;&gt;Presenting Twenty Seventeen&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;A brand new default theme brings your site to life with immersive featured images and video headers.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;alignnone wp-image-4618 size-large&quot; src=&quot;https://i2.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-Twenty-Seventeen-1.jpg?resize=632%2C356&amp;#038;ssl=1&quot; srcset=&quot;https://i2.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-Twenty-Seventeen-1.jpg?resize=1024%2C576&amp;amp;ssl=1 1024w, https://i2.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-Twenty-Seventeen-1.jpg?resize=300%2C169&amp;amp;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-Twenty-Seventeen-1.jpg?resize=768%2C432&amp;amp;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-Twenty-Seventeen-1.jpg?w=1600&amp;amp;ssl=1 1600w, https://i2.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-Twenty-Seventeen-1.jpg?w=1264&amp;amp;ssl=1 1264w&quot; sizes=&quot;(max-width: 632px) 100vw, 632px&quot; data-recalc-dims=&quot;1&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Twenty Seventeen focuses on business sites and features a customizable front page with multiple sections. Personalize it with widgets, navigation, social menus, a logo, custom colors, and more. Our default theme for 2017 works great in many languages, on any device, and for a wide range of users.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;hr /&gt;
&lt;h2 style=&quot;text-align:center&quot;&gt;Your Site, Your Way&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.7 adds new features to the customizer to help take you through the initial setup of a theme, with non-destructive live previews of all your changes in one uninterrupted workflow.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Theme Starter Content&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;div style=&quot;width: 632px;&quot; class=&quot;wp-video&quot;&gt;&lt;!--[if lt IE 9]&gt;&lt;script&gt;document.createElement('video');&lt;/script&gt;&lt;![endif]--&gt;
&lt;video class=&quot;wp-video-shortcode&quot; id=&quot;video-4596-1&quot; width=&quot;632&quot; height=&quot;346&quot; loop=&quot;1&quot; autoplay=&quot;1&quot; preload=&quot;metadata&quot; controls=&quot;controls&quot;&gt;&lt;source type=&quot;video/mp4&quot; src=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/starter-content.mp4?_=1&quot; /&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/starter-content.mp4&quot;&gt;https://wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/starter-content.mp4&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;To help give you a solid base to build from, individual themes can provide starter content that appears when you go to customize your brand new site. This can range from placing a business information widget in the best location to providing a sample menu with social icon links to a static front page complete with beautiful images. Don’t worry &amp;#8211; nothing new will appear on the live site until you’re ready to save and publish your initial theme setup.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div style=&quot;float: left;width: 48%;margin: 0&quot;&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Edit Shortcuts&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;div style=&quot;width: 300px;&quot; class=&quot;wp-video&quot;&gt;&lt;video class=&quot;wp-video-shortcode&quot; id=&quot;video-4596-2&quot; width=&quot;300&quot; height=&quot;173&quot; poster=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-Edit-Shortcuts.jpg&quot; loop=&quot;1&quot; autoplay=&quot;1&quot; preload=&quot;metadata&quot; controls=&quot;controls&quot;&gt;&lt;source type=&quot;video/mp4&quot; src=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/edit-shortcuts.mp4?_=2&quot; /&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/edit-shortcuts.mp4&quot;&gt;https://wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/edit-shortcuts.mp4&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Visible icons appear to show you which parts of your site can be customized while live previewing. Click on a shortcut and get straight to editing. Paired with starter content, getting started with customizing your site is faster than ever.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div style=&quot;float: right;width: 48%;margin: 0&quot;&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Video Headers&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;div style=&quot;width: 300px;&quot; class=&quot;wp-video&quot;&gt;&lt;video class=&quot;wp-video-shortcode&quot; id=&quot;video-4596-3&quot; width=&quot;300&quot; height=&quot;173&quot; poster=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-Header-Video.jpg&quot; loop=&quot;1&quot; autoplay=&quot;1&quot; preload=&quot;metadata&quot; controls=&quot;controls&quot;&gt;&lt;source type=&quot;video/mp4&quot; src=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/video-headers.mp4?_=3&quot; /&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/video-headers.mp4&quot;&gt;https://wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/video-headers.mp4&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Sometimes a big atmospheric video as a moving header image is just what you need to showcase your wares; go ahead and try it out with Twenty Seventeen. Need some video inspiration? Try searching for sites with video headers available for download and use.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div style=&quot;clear: both&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div style=&quot;float: left;width: 48%;margin: 0&quot;&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Smoother Menu Building&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;wp-image-4606 size-medium alignright&quot; src=&quot;https://i1.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-Nav.jpg?resize=300%2C158&amp;#038;ssl=1&quot; srcset=&quot;https://i1.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-Nav.jpg?resize=300%2C158&amp;amp;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-Nav.jpg?w=760&amp;amp;ssl=1 760w&quot; sizes=&quot;(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px&quot; data-recalc-dims=&quot;1&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Many menus for sites contain links to the pages of your site, but what happens when you don’t have any pages yet? Now you can add new pages while building menus instead of leaving the customizer and abandoning your changes. Once you’ve published your customizations, you’ll have new pages ready for you to fill with content.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div style=&quot;float: right;width: 48%;margin: 0&quot;&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Custom CSS&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;wp-image-4607 size-medium alignright&quot; src=&quot;https://i1.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-CSS.jpg?resize=300%2C158&amp;#038;ssl=1&quot; srcset=&quot;https://i1.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-CSS.jpg?resize=300%2C158&amp;amp;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-CSS.jpg?w=760&amp;amp;ssl=1 760w&quot; sizes=&quot;(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px&quot; data-recalc-dims=&quot;1&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Sometimes you just need a few visual tweaks to make your site perfect. WordPress 4.7 allows you to add custom CSS and instantly see how your changes affect your site. The live preview allows you to work quickly without page refreshes slowing you down.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div style=&quot;clear: both&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;hr /&gt;
&lt;div style=&quot;float: left;width: 48%;margin: 0&quot;&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;PDF Thumbnail Previews&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;wp-image-4609 size-medium alignright&quot; src=&quot;https://i1.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-PDF.jpg?resize=300%2C158&amp;#038;ssl=1&quot; srcset=&quot;https://i1.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-PDF.jpg?resize=300%2C158&amp;amp;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-PDF.jpg?w=760&amp;amp;ssl=1 760w&quot; sizes=&quot;(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px&quot; data-recalc-dims=&quot;1&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Managing your document collection is easier with WordPress 4.7. Uploading PDFs will generate thumbnail images so you can more easily distinguish between all your documents.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div style=&quot;float: right;width: 48%;margin: 0&quot;&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Dashboard in your language&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;wp-image-4608 size-medium alignright&quot; src=&quot;https://i2.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-Language.jpg?resize=300%2C158&amp;#038;ssl=1&quot; srcset=&quot;https://i2.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-Language.jpg?resize=300%2C158&amp;amp;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-Language.jpg?w=760&amp;amp;ssl=1 760w&quot; sizes=&quot;(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px&quot; data-recalc-dims=&quot;1&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Just because your site is in one language doesn’t mean that everybody helping manage it prefers that language for their admin. Add more languages to your site and a user language option will show up in your user’s profiles.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;div style=&quot;clear: both&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;hr /&gt;
&lt;h2 style=&quot;text-align:center&quot;&gt;Introducing REST API Content Endpoints&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.7 comes with REST API endpoints for posts, comments, terms, users, meta, and settings.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-large wp-image-4600 alignnone&quot; src=&quot;https://i2.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-API.jpg?resize=632%2C205&amp;#038;ssl=1&quot; alt=&quot;&quot; srcset=&quot;https://i2.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-API.jpg?resize=1024%2C332&amp;amp;ssl=1 1024w, https://i2.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-API.jpg?resize=300%2C97&amp;amp;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-API.jpg?resize=768%2C249&amp;amp;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-API.jpg?w=1264&amp;amp;ssl=1 1264w, https://i2.wp.com/wordpress.org/news/files/2016/12/4.7-—-API.jpg?w=1896&amp;amp;ssl=1 1896w&quot; sizes=&quot;(max-width: 632px) 100vw, 632px&quot; data-recalc-dims=&quot;1&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Content endpoints provide machine-readable external access to your WordPress site with a clear, standards-driven interface, paving the way for new and innovative methods of interacting with sites through plugins, themes, apps, and beyond. Ready to get started with development? &lt;a href=&quot;https://developer.wordpress.org/rest-api/reference/&quot;&gt;Check out the REST API reference.&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;hr /&gt;
&lt;h2 style=&quot;text-align:center&quot;&gt;Even More Developer Happiness &lt;img src=&quot;https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/2.2.1/72x72/1f60a.png&quot; alt=&quot;?&quot; class=&quot;wp-smiley&quot; style=&quot;height: 1em; max-height: 1em;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/11/03/post-type-templates-in-4-7/&quot;&gt;Post Type Templates&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;By opening up the page template functionality to all post types, theme developers have even more flexibility with the WordPress template hierarchy.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;More Theme API Goodies&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.7 includes &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/09/09/new-functions-hooks-and-behaviour-for-theme-developers-in-wordpress-4-7/&quot;&gt;new functions, hooks, and behavior&lt;/a&gt; for theme developers.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/10/04/custom-bulk-actions/&quot;&gt;Custom Bulk Actions&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;List tables, now with more than bulk edit and delete.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/09/08/wp_hook-next-generation-actions-and-filters/&quot;&gt;&lt;code&gt;WP_Hook&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The code that lies beneath actions and filters has been overhauled and modernized, fixing bugs along the way.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Settings Registration API&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;register_setting() &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/10/26/registering-your-settings-in-wordpress-4-7/&quot;&gt;has been enhanced&lt;/a&gt; to include type, description, and REST API visibility.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/10/12/customize-changesets-technical-design-decisions/&quot;&gt;Customize Changesets&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Customize changesets make changes in the customizer persistent, like autosave drafts. They also make exciting new features like starter content possible.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;hr /&gt;

			&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:4:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:6:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:17:&quot;Moving Toward SSL&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:53:&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/12/moving-toward-ssl/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 01 Dec 2016 17:20:29 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;category&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:11:&quot;Development&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:34:&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/?p=4588&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:1:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:1:{s:11:&quot;isPermaLink&quot;;s:5:&quot;false&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:327:&quot;We’re at a turning point: 2017 is going to be the year that we’re going to see features in WordPress which require hosts to have HTTPS available. Just as JavaScript is a near necessity for smoother user experiences and more modern PHP versions are critical for performance, SSL just makes sense as the next hurdle [&amp;#8230;]&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:14:&quot;Matt Mullenweg&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:40:&quot;http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;encoded&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1627:&quot;&lt;p&gt;We’re at a turning point: 2017 is going to be the year that we’re going to see features in WordPress which require hosts to have HTTPS available. Just as JavaScript is a near necessity for smoother user experiences and more modern PHP versions are critical for performance, SSL just makes sense as the next hurdle our users are going to face.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;SSL basically means the link between your browser and the server is encrypted. SSL used to be difficult to implement, and often expensive or slow. Modern browsers, and the incredible success of projects like &lt;a href=&quot;https://letsencrypt.org/&quot;&gt;Let&amp;#8217;s Encrypt&lt;/a&gt; have made getting a certificate to secure your site fast, free, and something we think every host should support by default, especially in a post-Snowden era. Google also weighs &lt;a href=&quot;https://security.googleblog.com/2014/08/https-as-ranking-signal_6.html&quot;&gt;SSL as a search engine ranking factor&lt;/a&gt; and will begin &lt;a href=&quot;http://motherboard.vice.com/read/google-will-soon-shame-all-websites-that-are-unencrypted-chrome-https&quot;&gt;flagging unencrypted sites in Chrome&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;First, early in 2017, we will only promote hosting partners that provide a SSL certificate by default in their accounts. Later we will begin to assess which features, such as API authentication, would benefit the most from SSL and make them only enabled when SSL is there.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Separately, I also think the performance improvements in PHP7 are particularly impressive, and major kudos to everyone who worked on that. We will consider whether hosts use PHP7 by default for new accounts next year as well.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;

RC means we think we’re done, but with millions of users and thousands of plugins and themes, it’s possible we’ve missed something. We hope to ship WordPress 4.7 on Tuesday, December 6, but we need your help to get there. If you haven’t tested 4.7 yet, [&amp;#8230;]&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:15:&quot;Helen Hou-Sandi&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:40:&quot;http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;encoded&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4331:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The release candidate for WordPress 4.7 is now available.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;RC means we think we’re done, but with millions of users and thousands of plugins and themes, it’s possible we’ve missed something. We hope to ship WordPress 4.7 on &lt;strong&gt;Tuesday, December 6&lt;/strong&gt;, but we need &lt;em&gt;your&lt;/em&gt; help to get there. If you haven’t tested 4.7 yet, now is the time! To test WordPress 4.7, you can use the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/plugins/wordpress-beta-tester/&quot;&gt;WordPress Beta Tester&lt;/a&gt; plugin or you can &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/wordpress-4.7-RC1.zip&quot;&gt;download the release candidate here&lt;/a&gt; (zip).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.7 is a jam-packed release, with a number of features focused on getting a theme set up for the first time. Highlights include a &lt;a href=&quot;http://2017.wordpress.net/&quot;&gt;new default theme&lt;/a&gt;, video headers, custom CSS, customizer edit shortcuts, PDF thumbnail previews, user admin languages, REST API content endpoints, post type templates, and more.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We’ve made &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/log/trunk/src?action=stop_on_copy&amp;amp;mode=stop_on_copy&amp;amp;rev=39353&amp;amp;stop_rev=39263&amp;amp;limit=200&amp;amp;verbose=on&amp;amp;sfp_email=&amp;amp;sfph_mail=&quot;&gt;quite a few refinements&lt;/a&gt; since releasing Beta 4 a week ago, including usability and accessibility enhancements for video headers, media and page template support in starter content, and polishing of how custom CSS can be migrated to and extended by plugins and themes. The REST API endpoints saw a number of bugfixes and notably now have anonymous comment off by default.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Not sure where to start with testing? Try setting up a fresh site on a new installation with Twenty Seventeen (hint: head into customizing your site before touching any pages or widgets) and taking notes on what you enjoyed and what got you stuck. For more details about what&amp;#8217;s new in version 4.7, check out the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/10/wordpress-4-7-beta-1/&quot;&gt;Beta 1&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/11/wordpress-4-7-beta-2/&quot;&gt;Beta 2&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/11/wordpress-4-7-beta-3/&quot;&gt;Beta 3&lt;/a&gt;, and &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/11/wordpress-4-7-beta-4/&quot;&gt;Beta 4&lt;/a&gt; blog posts.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Think you’ve found a bug?&lt;/strong&gt; Please post to the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/support/forum/alphabeta/&quot;&gt;Alpha/Beta support forum&lt;/a&gt;. If any known issues come up, you’ll be able to &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/report/5&quot;&gt;find them here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Developers&lt;/strong&gt;, please test your plugins and themes against WordPress 4.7 and update your plugin’s &lt;em&gt;Tested up to&lt;/em&gt; version in the readme to 4.7. If you find compatibility problems please be sure to post to the support forums so we can figure those out before the final release – we work hard to avoid breaking things. An in-depth field guide to developer-focused changes is coming soon on the &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/&quot;&gt;core development blog&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Do you speak a language other than English? &lt;a href=&quot;https://translate.wordpress.org/projects/wp/dev&quot;&gt;Help us translate WordPress into more than 100 languages!&lt;/a&gt; And if you haven&amp;#8217;t yet done so, now is a great time to &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpressdotorg.polldaddy.com/s/wordpress-2016-survey&quot;&gt;take the Annual WordPress Survey&lt;/a&gt; and send it on to your friends.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Happy testing! And now for another &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/ramiabraham&quot;&gt;Rami Abraham&lt;/a&gt; haiku break.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Select your language&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;em&gt;Then let your users choose theirs&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;em&gt;&lt;code&gt;get_user_locale()&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Theme authors rejoice&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Custom header video&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;em&gt;Make sure to &lt;code&gt;add_theme_support&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;em&gt;Bling above the fold&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;This software is still in development,&lt;/strong&gt; so we don’t recommend you run it on a production site. Consider setting up a test site just to play with the new version. To test WordPress 4.7, try the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/plugins/wordpress-beta-tester/&quot;&gt;WordPress Beta Tester&lt;/a&gt; plugin (you’ll want “bleeding edge nightlies”). Or you can &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/wordpress-4.7-beta4.zip&quot;&gt;download the beta here&lt;/a&gt; (zip).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;For more information on what’s new in 4.7, check out the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/10/wordpress-4-7-beta-1/&quot;&gt;Beta 1,&lt;/a&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/11/wordpress-4-7-beta-2/&quot;&gt;Beta 2&lt;/a&gt;, and &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/11/wordpress-4-7-beta-3/&quot;&gt;Beta 3&lt;/a&gt; blog posts, along with &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/tag/4-7+dev-notes/&quot;&gt;in-depth developer guides on make/core&lt;/a&gt;. We’ve made &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/log/trunk/src?action=stop_on_copy&amp;amp;mode=stop_on_copy&amp;amp;rev=39262&amp;amp;stop_rev=39201&amp;amp;limit=200&amp;amp;verbose=on&amp;amp;sfp_email=&amp;amp;sfph_mail=&quot;&gt;about 60 changes&lt;/a&gt; in the last few days for beta 4, including tweaks to Twenty Seventeen, custom CSS, and the REST API content endpoints.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Do you speak a language other than English? &lt;a href=&quot;https://translate.wordpress.org/projects/wp/dev&quot;&gt;Help us translate WordPress into more than 100 languages!&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;If you think you’ve found a bug&lt;/strong&gt;, you can post to the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/support/forum/alphabeta&quot;&gt;Alpha/Beta area&lt;/a&gt; in the support forums. We’d love to hear from you! If you’re comfortable writing a reproducible bug report, &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/reports/&quot;&gt;file one on WordPress Trac&lt;/a&gt;, where you can also find &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/tickets/major&quot;&gt;a list of known bugs&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;We are almost there&lt;br /&gt;
Please test your plugins and themes&lt;br /&gt;
RC coming soon&lt;br /&gt;

&lt;p&gt;The title says it all. We had some great applications for cities to host &lt;a href=&quot;http://us.wordcamp.org/&quot;&gt;WordCamp US&lt;/a&gt; after we finish up in Philadelphia this year, and the city chosen for 2017-2018 is &lt;strong&gt;Nashville, Tennessee&lt;/strong&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Based on the other great applications we got I&amp;#8217;m also excited about the pipeline of communities that could host it in future years as WordCamp US travels across the United States and gives us an opportunity to learn and love a new city, as we have with Philadelphia.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;By the way, if you haven&amp;#8217;t yet, now is a great time to &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpressdotorg.polldaddy.com/s/wordpress-2016-survey&quot;&gt;take the Annual WordPress Survey&lt;/a&gt; and ask your friends to as well.&lt;/p&gt;

This software is still in development, so we don’t recommend you run it on a production site. Consider setting up a test site just to play with the new version. To test WordPress 4.7, try the WordPress Beta Tester plugin (you’ll want “bleeding edge nightlies”). Or you can [&amp;#8230;]&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:15:&quot;Helen Hou-Sandi&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:40:&quot;http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;encoded&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3120:&quot;&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.7 Beta 3 is now available!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;This software is still in development,&lt;/strong&gt; so we don’t recommend you run it on a production site. Consider setting up a test site just to play with the new version. To test WordPress 4.7, try the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/plugins/wordpress-beta-tester/&quot;&gt;WordPress Beta Tester&lt;/a&gt; plugin (you’ll want “bleeding edge nightlies”). Or you can &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/wordpress-4.7-beta3.zip&quot;&gt;download the beta here&lt;/a&gt; (zip).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;For more information on what’s new in 4.7, check out the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/10/wordpress-4-7-beta-1/&quot;&gt;Beta 1&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/11/wordpress-4-7-beta-2/&quot;&gt;Beta 2&lt;/a&gt; blog posts, along with &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/tag/4-7+dev-notes/&quot;&gt;in-depth field guides on make/core&lt;/a&gt;. Some of the changes in Beta 3 include:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;REST API:&lt;/strong&gt; The &lt;code&gt;unfiltered_html&lt;/code&gt; capability is now respected and &lt;code&gt;rest_base&lt;/code&gt; has been added to response objects of &lt;code&gt;wp/v2/taxonomies&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;wp/v2/types&lt;/code&gt;, while &lt;code&gt;get_allowed_query_vars()&lt;/code&gt; and the &lt;code&gt;rest_get_post&lt;/code&gt; filter have been removed.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Roles/Capabilities:&lt;/strong&gt; Added meta-caps for comment, term, and user meta, which are currently only used in the REST API.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;I18N:&lt;/strong&gt; Added the ability to change user&amp;#8217;s locale back to site&amp;#8217;s locale. (&lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/38632&quot;&gt;#38632&lt;/a&gt;)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Custom CSS:&lt;/strong&gt; Renamed the &lt;code&gt;unfiltered_css&lt;/code&gt; meta capability to &lt;code&gt;edit_css&lt;/code&gt; and added revisions support to the &lt;code&gt;custom_css&lt;/code&gt; post type.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Edit shortcuts:&lt;/strong&gt; Theme authors should take a look at &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/11/10/visible-edit-shortcuts-in-the-customizer-preview/&quot;&gt;the developer guide to the customizer preview&amp;#8217;s visible edit shortcuts&lt;/a&gt; and update their themes to take advantage of them if not already implementing selective refresh.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Various bug fixes:&lt;/strong&gt; We’ve made &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/log/trunk/src?action=stop_on_copy&amp;amp;mode=stop_on_copy&amp;amp;rev=39200&amp;amp;stop_rev=39143&amp;amp;limit=200&amp;amp;verbose=on&amp;amp;sfp_email=&amp;amp;sfph_mail=&quot;&gt;over 50 changes&lt;/a&gt; in the last week.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Do you speak a language other than English? &lt;a href=&quot;https://translate.wordpress.org/projects/wp/dev&quot;&gt;Help us translate WordPress into more than 100 languages!&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;If you think you’ve found a bug&lt;/strong&gt;, you can post to the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/support/forum/alphabeta&quot;&gt;Alpha/Beta area&lt;/a&gt; in the support forums. We’d love to hear from you! If you’re comfortable writing a reproducible bug report, &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/reports/&quot;&gt;file one on WordPress Trac&lt;/a&gt;, where you can also find &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/tickets/major&quot;&gt;a list of known bugs&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Building the future&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;em&gt;A global community&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;em&gt;Stronger together&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

+0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;category&quot;;a:3:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:11:&quot;Development&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}i:1;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:8:&quot;Releases&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}i:2;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3:&quot;4.7&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:34:&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/?p=4552&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:1:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:1:{s:11:&quot;isPermaLink&quot;;s:5:&quot;false&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:329:&quot;WordPress Or you can [&amp;#8230;]&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:15:&quot;Helen Hou-Sandi&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:40:&quot;http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;encoded&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4240:&quot;&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.7 Beta 2 is now available!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;This software is still in development,&lt;/strong&gt; so we don’t recommend you run it on a production site. Consider setting up a test site just to play with the new version. To test WordPress 4.7, try the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/plugins/wordpress-beta-tester/&quot;&gt;WordPress Beta Tester&lt;/a&gt; plugin (you’ll want “bleeding edge nightlies”). Or you can &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/wordpress-4.7-beta2.zip&quot;&gt;download the beta here&lt;/a&gt; (zip).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Notable changes since WordPress 4.7 Beta 1:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Twenty Seventeen:&lt;/strong&gt; The theme wasn&amp;#8217;t being installed on upgrades &amp;#8211; sorry about that! Now you should see it if you&amp;#8217;re upgrading an existing site. There are also plenty of fixes, especially for the header and small screen views.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Edit shortcuts:&lt;/strong&gt; These are always visible while editing (hide them on bigger screens by collapsing the controls) and should now work properly in Firefox. (&lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/27403&quot;&gt;#27403&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/38532&quot;&gt;#38532&lt;/a&gt;)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;REST API endpoints:&lt;/strong&gt; There have been a number of changes over the past week; your attention is requested on the following:
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;The &lt;code&gt;DELETE&lt;/code&gt; response format has changed and may need to be accounted for. (&lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/38494&quot;&gt;#38494&lt;/a&gt;)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Enabled querying by multiple post statuses. (&lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/38420&quot;&gt;#38420&lt;/a&gt;)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Return an error when JSON decoding fails. (&lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/38547&quot;&gt;#38547&lt;/a&gt;)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;More developer notes&lt;/strong&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/10/28/fine-grained-capabilities-for-taxonomy-terms-in-4-7/&quot;&gt;Fine grained capabilities for taxonomy terms&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/10/29/wp_taxonomy-in-4-7/&quot;&gt;&lt;code&gt;WP_Taxonomy&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/11/02/wp_list_sort-and-wp_list_util-in-4-7/&quot;&gt;&lt;code&gt;wp_list_sort()&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;WP_List_Util&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/11/03/post-type-templates-in-4-7/&quot;&gt;Post type templates&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/11/03/new-post-type-labels-in-4-7/&quot;&gt;New post type labels&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/11/03/attributes-for-resource-hints-in-4-7/&quot;&gt;Attributes for resource hints&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Various bug fixes:&lt;/strong&gt; We’ve made &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/log/trunk/src?action=stop_on_copy&amp;amp;mode=stop_on_copy&amp;amp;rev=39142&amp;amp;stop_rev=38995&amp;amp;limit=200&amp;amp;verbose=on&amp;amp;sfp_email=&amp;amp;sfph_mail=&quot;&gt;almost 150 changes&lt;/a&gt; in the last week.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;For more of what’s new in version 4.7, &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/10/wordpress-4-7-beta-1/&quot;&gt;check out the Beta 1 blog post&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you want a more in-depth view of what major changes have made it into 4.7, &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/tag/4-7/&quot;&gt;check out posts tagged with 4.7 on the main development blog&lt;/a&gt;, or look at a &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/query?status=closed&amp;amp;resolution=fixed&amp;amp;milestone=4.7&amp;amp;group=component&amp;amp;order=priority&quot;&gt;list of everything&lt;/a&gt; that’s changed. There will be more developer notes to come, so keep an eye out for those as well.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Do you speak a language other than English? &lt;a href=&quot;https://translate.wordpress.org/projects/wp/dev&quot;&gt;Help us translate WordPress into more than 100 languages!&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;If you think you’ve found a bug&lt;/strong&gt;, you can post to the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/support/forum/alphabeta&quot;&gt;Alpha/Beta area&lt;/a&gt; in the support forums. We’d love to hear from you! If you’re comfortable writing a reproducible bug report, &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/reports/&quot;&gt;file one on WordPress Trac&lt;/a&gt;, where you can also find &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/tickets/major&quot;&gt;a list of known bugs&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Happy testing!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Ya es la hora&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;em&gt; Time for another beta&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
请您帮下忙!&lt;/p&gt;

+0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;category&quot;;a:3:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:11:&quot;Development&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}i:1;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:8:&quot;Releases&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}i:2;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3:&quot;4.7&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:34:&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/?p=4535&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:1:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:1:{s:11:&quot;isPermaLink&quot;;s:5:&quot;false&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:329:&quot;WordPress This software is still in development, so we don’t recommend you run it on a production site. Consider setting up a test site just to play with the new version. To test WordPress 4.7, try the WordPress Beta Tester plugin (you’ll want “bleeding edge nightlies”). Or you can [&amp;#8230;]&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:15:&quot;Helen Hou-Sandi&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:40:&quot;http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;encoded&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:6895:&quot;&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.7 Beta 1 is now available!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;This software is still in development,&lt;/strong&gt; so we don’t recommend you run it on a production site. Consider setting up a test site just to play with the new version. To test WordPress 4.7, try the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/plugins/wordpress-beta-tester/&quot;&gt;WordPress Beta Tester&lt;/a&gt; plugin (you’ll want “bleeding edge nightlies”). Or you can &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/wordpress-4.7-beta1.zip&quot;&gt;download the beta here&lt;/a&gt; (zip).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.7 is slated for release on &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/4-7/&quot;&gt;December 6&lt;/a&gt;, but we need your help to get there. We&amp;#8217;ve been working on a lot of things, many of them to make getting your site set up the way you want it much easier. Here are some of the bigger items to test and help us find as many bugs as possible in the coming weeks:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://2017.wordpress.net/&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Twenty Seventeen&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8211; A brand new default theme brings your site to life with immersive featured images, video headers, and subtle animations. With a focus on business sites, it features multiple sections on the front page as well as widgets, navigation and social menus, a logo, and more. Personalize its asymmetrical grid with a custom color scheme and showcase your multimedia content with post formats. Our default theme for 2017 works great in many languages, for any abilities, and on any device.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Video Headers&lt;/strong&gt; &amp;#8211; Sometimes a big atmospheric video as a moving header image is just what you need to showcase your wares; go ahead and try it out with Twenty Seventeen. Need some video inspiration? Try searching for sites with video headers available for download and use.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Set up your site in one flow&lt;/strong&gt; &amp;#8211; From finding and installing themes right inside the customizer, to automatically staged theme-specific starter content, to clickable shortcuts that jump directly to editing an item from the preview pane, to adding pages while you&amp;#8217;re building a nav menu or setting a static front page: getting a new site spun up and ready to share with a friend or a coworker is faster and easier than it&amp;#8217;s ever been. Note: starter content appears when live previewing brand new sites and is currently only available in Twenty Seventeen. We&amp;#8217;ll be expanding this to other bundled themes very soon, and perhaps to sites with existing content in future releases of WordPress.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Custom CSS with live previews&lt;/strong&gt; &amp;#8211; Ever needed to hide or tweak the look of something in your theme or from a plugin? Now you can do it with CSS and live preview the results while customizing your site. CSS can be a powerful tool; you may find that you won&amp;#8217;t need the theme editor or child themes anymore.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;User admin languages&lt;/strong&gt; &amp;#8211; Just because your site is in one language doesn&amp;#8217;t mean that everybody helping manage it prefers that language for their admin. To try this out, you&amp;#8217;ll need to have more than one language installed, which will make a user language option available in your profile.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;PDF thumbnail previews&lt;/strong&gt; &amp;#8211; Uploading PDFs will now generate thumbnail images so you can more easily distinguish between all your documents.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;As always, there have been exciting changes for developers to explore as well, such as:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;REST API content endpoints&lt;/strong&gt; &amp;#8211; If you only test one thing as a developer, please test these. This phase is particularly helpful for people building plugins, themes, and in-admin interfaces. Can you build the things you need? Are these ready for release, and is the world ready for them? (&lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/38373&quot;&gt;#38373&lt;/a&gt;)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;code&gt;WP_Hook&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; &amp;#8211; The code that lies beneath actions and filters has been overhauled. You likely aren&amp;#8217;t affected, but if you&amp;#8217;ve done things to the &lt;code&gt;$wp_filter&lt;/code&gt; global or experienced funky recursion bugs in the past, &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/09/08/wp_hook-next-generation-actions-and-filters/&quot;&gt;please take a moment to read the dev note&lt;/a&gt; and test your code.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/10/04/custom-bulk-actions/&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Custom bulk actions&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8211; List tables, now with more than bulk edit and delete.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Expanded &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/10/26/registering-your-settings-in-wordpress-4-7/&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Settings Registration API&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/a&gt; via &lt;code&gt;register_setting()&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;For theme developers: &lt;strong&gt;Post type templates&lt;/strong&gt; (&lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/18375&quot;&gt;#18375&lt;/a&gt;)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/09/09/new-functions-hooks-and-behaviour-for-theme-developers-in-wordpress-4-7/&quot;&gt;More goodies for theme developers!&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Locale switching&lt;/strong&gt; (&lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/26511&quot;&gt;#26511&lt;/a&gt;)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/10/11/comment-allowed-checks-in-wordpress-4-7/&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Comment allowed checks&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/a&gt; have the potential for a back-compat break.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you want a more in-depth view of what major changes have made it into 4.7, &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/tag/4-7/&quot;&gt;check out posts tagged with 4.7 on the main development blog&lt;/a&gt;, or look at a &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/query?status=closed&amp;amp;resolution=fixed&amp;amp;milestone=4.7&amp;amp;group=component&amp;amp;order=priority&quot;&gt;list of everything&lt;/a&gt; that’s changed. There will be more developer notes to come, so keep an eye out for those as well.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;If you think you’ve found a bug&lt;/strong&gt;, you can post to the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/support/forum/alphabeta&quot;&gt;Alpha/Beta area&lt;/a&gt; in the support forums. We’d love to hear from you! If you’re comfortable writing a reproducible bug report, &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/reports/&quot;&gt;file one on WordPress Trac&lt;/a&gt;, where you can also find &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/tickets/major&quot;&gt;a list of known bugs&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Happy testing, and please enjoy this extended haiku break, courtesy of &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/ramiabraham&quot;&gt;Rami Abraham&lt;/a&gt;&lt;em&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Exquisite endpoints&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;em&gt;Extol epic exabytes&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;em&gt;Enabling earthlings&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Careful interfaces&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;em&gt;Considerately conjured&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;em&gt;Customizer chic&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Ring in the new year&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;em&gt;With elegance and balance&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;em&gt;Twenty Seventeen&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Hooks hook healthily&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;

&lt;em&gt;Sane iterations&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Admin in your tongue&lt;br /&gt;

We all speak WordPress&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

wordpress translation day&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}i:3;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:9:&quot;polyglots&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}i:4;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;translations&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:34:&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/?p=4516&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:1:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:1:{s:11:&quot;isPermaLink&quot;;s:5:&quot;false&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:373:&quot;The WordPress Polyglots team is organizing the second Global WordPress Translation Day on November 12th. Everyone is invited to join – from anywhere in the world! Translating is one of the easiest ways to get involved with WordPress and contribute to the project. Global WordPress Translation Day is your chance to learn more about translating WordPress, meet [&amp;#8230;]&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:15:&quot;Petya Raykovska&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:40:&quot;http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;encoded&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4273:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The WordPress Polyglots team is organizing the second &lt;a href=&quot;https://wptranslationday.org/&quot;&gt;Global WordPress Translation Day&lt;/a&gt; on November 12th. Everyone is invited to join – from anywhere in the world!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Translating is one of the easiest ways to get involved with WordPress and contribute to the project. Global WordPress Translation Day is your chance to learn more about translating WordPress, meet people from all over the world, and &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/polyglots/teams&quot;&gt;translate WordPress into one of more than 160 languages&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Join us on November 12th from anywhere in the world&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The translation day starts on Saturday, November 12th, 2016, at 0:00 UTC and ends 24 hours later. &lt;a href=&quot;http://arewemeetingyet.com/UTC/2016-11-12/00:00/Global%20WordPress%20Translation%20Day%202&quot;&gt;See what time that is for you!&lt;/a&gt; You can join right from the start, or any time it&amp;#8217;s convenient for you throughout the day.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;What are we doing?&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Local contributor days are happening all over the world, and are a great way to get involved. &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.google.com/maps/d/viewer?mid=12Gni4JMfShyWHPqGNwh5-PMneMM&amp;amp;usp=sharing&quot;&gt;Check out this map&lt;/a&gt; to see if there&amp;#8217;s already a local event happening near you. Can&amp;#8217;t find one? &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/polyglots/2016/09/22/global-wordpress-translation-day-2-on-november-12th-2016/&quot;&gt;Organize a local event!&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;At the same time, &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.crowdcast.io/e/gwtd2/register&quot;&gt;join the community for 24 hours of live-streamed, remote sessions&lt;/a&gt; in numerous languages. Sessions will cover localization, internationalization, and contributing in your language.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Who&amp;#8217;s it for?&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Whether you&amp;#8217;re new to translating and want to learn how to translate, or an experienced translation editor building a strong team, the translation day is for &lt;i&gt;you&lt;/i&gt;. Developers will also enjoy topics from experienced contributors, whether you&amp;#8217;re learning about internationalization and or want to find more translators for your themes and plugins. There&amp;#8217;s a session for everyone!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Get Involved&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Joining is easy! On November 12th, in your own timezone, &lt;a href=&quot;https://translate.wordpress.org&quot;&gt;translate WordPress&lt;/a&gt; or your favorite plugins and themes into your language, while watching live sessions over the course of the day.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Want to get more involved? &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/polyglots/2016/09/22/global-wordpress-translation-day-2-on-november-12th-2016/&quot;&gt;Sign up to organize a local event&lt;/a&gt; and invite your local community to translate together on November 12th. Events can be formal or completely informal – grab your laptop and a couple of friends, and head to a local coffee shop to translate for an hour or two.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Can you get involved if you only speak English?&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Absolutely! Even if you only speak English, there are great sessions about internationalization that can benefit every developer. There&amp;#8217;s also lots of English variants that need your help! For example, English is spoken and written differently in Australia, Canada, New Zealand, South Africa, and the United Kingdom. You can learn about these differences and why these variants are important during the sessions.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;And if you’re feeling fun, try translating WordPress into emoji! Yep, we have a translation of WordPress in emoji! &lt;img src=&quot;https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/2.2.1/72x72/1f30e.png&quot; alt=&quot;?&quot; class=&quot;wp-smiley&quot; style=&quot;height: 1em; max-height: 1em;&quot; /&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/2.2.1/72x72/1f30d.png&quot; alt=&quot;?&quot; class=&quot;wp-smiley&quot; style=&quot;height: 1em; max-height: 1em;&quot; /&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/2.2.1/72x72/1f30f.png&quot; alt=&quot;?&quot; class=&quot;wp-smiley&quot; style=&quot;height: 1em; max-height: 1em;&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Questions?&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you have any questions, the polyglots team and the event organizers hang out in &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.slack.com/messages/polyglots/&quot;&gt;#polyglots in Slack&lt;/a&gt; and are happy to help! (Get an invite to Slack at &lt;a href=&quot;https://chat.wordpress.org&quot;&gt;chat.wordpress.org&lt;/a&gt;.)&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Sign up to take part in the event on the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wptranslationday.org/&quot;&gt;official website&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

+0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;category&quot;;a:3:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:8:&quot;Releases&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}i:1;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:8:&quot;Security&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}i:2;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3:&quot;4.6&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:34:&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/?p=4507&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:1:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:1:{s:11:&quot;isPermaLink&quot;;s:5:&quot;false&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:377:&quot;WordPress 4.6.1 is now available. This is a security release for all previous versions and we strongly encourage you to update your sites immediately. WordPress versions 4.6 and earlier are affected by two security issues: a cross-site scripting vulnerability via image filename, reported by SumOfPwn researcher Cengiz Han Sahin; and a path traversal vulnerability in [&amp;#8230;]&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:11:&quot;Jeremy Felt&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:40:&quot;http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;encoded&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:2757:&quot;&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.6.1 is now available. This is a &lt;strong&gt;security release&lt;/strong&gt; for all previous versions and we strongly encourage you to update your sites immediately.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress versions 4.6 and earlier are affected by two security issues: a cross-site scripting vulnerability via image filename, reported by SumOfPwn researcher &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/cengizhansahin&quot;&gt;Cengiz Han Sahin&lt;/a&gt;; and a path traversal vulnerability in the upgrade package uploader, reported by &lt;a href=&quot;https://dominikschilling.de/&quot;&gt;Dominik Schilling&lt;/a&gt; from the WordPress security team.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Thank you to the reporters for practicing &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/handbook/testing/reporting-security-vulnerabilities/&quot;&gt;responsible disclosure&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In addition to the security issues above, WordPress 4.6.1 fixes 15 bugs from 4.6. For more information, see the &lt;a href=&quot;https://codex.wordpress.org/Version_4.6.1&quot;&gt;release notes&lt;/a&gt; or consult the &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/query?milestone=4.6.1&quot;&gt;list of changes&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/download/&quot;&gt;Download WordPress 4.6.1&lt;/a&gt; or venture over to Dashboard → Updates and simply click “Update Now.” Sites that support automatic background updates are already beginning to update to WordPress 4.6.1.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Thanks to everyone who contributed to 4.6.1:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/azaozz&quot;&gt;Andrew Ozz&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/gitlost&quot;&gt;bonger&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/boonebgorges&quot;&gt;Boone Gorges&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/chaos-engine&quot;&gt;Chaos Engine&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/danielkanchev&quot;&gt;Daniel Kanchev&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/dd32&quot;&gt;Dion Hulse&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/drewapicture&quot;&gt;Drew Jaynes&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/flixos90&quot;&gt;Felix Arntz&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/frozzare&quot;&gt;Fredrik Forsmo&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/pento&quot;&gt;Gary Pendergast&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/geminorum&quot;&gt;geminorum&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/iandunn&quot;&gt;Ian Dunn&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/ionutst&quot;&gt;Ionut Stanciu&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/jeremyfelt&quot;&gt;Jeremy Felt&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/joemcgill&quot;&gt;Joe McGill&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/clorith&quot;&gt;Marius L. &quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:30:&quot;com-wordpress:feed-additions:1&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;post-id&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4:&quot;4507&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}}}s:27:&quot;http://www.w3.org/2005/Atom&quot;;a:1:{s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:1:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:3:{s:4:&quot;href&quot;;s:32:&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/feed/&quot;;s:3:&quot;rel&quot;;s:4:&quot;self&quot;;s:4:&quot;type&quot;;s:19:&quot;application/rss+xml&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:44:&quot;http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/syndication/&quot;;a:2:{s:12:&quot;updatePeriod&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:6:&quot;hourly&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:15:&quot;updateFrequency&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1:&quot;1&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:30:&quot;com-wordpress:feed-additions:1&quot;;a:1:{s:4:&quot;site&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:8:&quot;14607090&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}}}}}}}}s:4:&quot;type&quot;;i:128;s:7:&quot;headers&quot;;O:42:&quot;Requests_Utility_CaseInsensitiveDictionary&quot;:1:{s:7:&quot; * data&quot;;a:9:{s:6:&quot;server&quot;;s:5:&quot;nginx&quot;;s:4:&quot;date&quot;;s:29:&quot;Wed, &quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:1:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:16:&quot;WordPress Planet&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://planet.wordpress.org/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;language&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:2:&quot;en&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:47:&quot;WordPress Planet - http://planet.wordpress.org/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;item&quot;;a:50:{i:0;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:135:&quot;WPTavern: State of the Word 2016: Mullenweg Pushes Calypso as Future of WordPress’ Interface, Proposes Major Changes to Release Cycle&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:29:&quot;https://wptavern.com/?p=64185&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:141:&quot;https://wptavern.com/state-of-the-word-2016-mullenweg-pushes-calypso-as-future-of-wordpress-interface-proposes-major-changes-to-release-cycle&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:14787:&quot;&lt;a href=&quot;https://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/sotw-2016.jpg?ssl=1&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;https://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/sotw-2016.jpg?resize=1025%2C487&amp;ssl=1&quot; alt=&quot;photo credit: WordCamp US organizing team&quot; class=&quot;size-full wp-image-64217&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;photo credit: &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/WordCampUS/status/805156416935882752&quot;&gt;WordCamp US organizing team&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Philadelphia welcomed 1,923 attendees to WordCamp US this weekend with an additional 2,028 enthusiasts watching via live stream. Matt Mullenweg delivered his 11th annual State of the Word address to a rapt audience ready to celebrate WordPress&amp;#8217; progress over the past year and hear the project leader&amp;#8217;s vision for 2017.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;He began by thanking sponsors and volunteers who made the event possible by covering the bulk of the $516 actual cost per person. Mullenweg said sponsors cover roughly 85-95% of the cost of WordCamps worldwide. In 2016, the events sold a total 36,000 tickets, with costs subsidized by more than 1,000 sponsors.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Mullenweg said meetups are the leading indicator for WordCamps and these events have had the fastest growth the community has seen in five or six years. More than 62,566 people attended a local meetup in 58 countries and roughly one third of those were new members.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot;&gt;&lt;p lang=&quot;en&quot; dir=&quot;ltr&quot;&gt;It’s been a great year for WordCamps and meetups &amp;#8211; 115 total WordCamps hosted in 41 different countries. &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/hashtag/wcus?src=hash&quot;&gt;#wcus&lt;/a&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;https://t.co/yVGkT0j52C&quot;&gt;pic.twitter.com/yVGkT0j52C&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;mdash; WordCamp US (@WordCampUS) &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/WordCampUS/status/805156784763715584&quot;&gt;December 3, 2016&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;WordPress Foundation to Create WordPress Community Support Subsidiary&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In order to better accommodate the extraordinary growth of the global community, the WordPress Foundation will be restructuring its management of WordCamps. In 2016 the Foundation took in an estimated $4.3 million, up from $2.8 million in 2015, with 99.9% of those funds related to WordCamps. Mullenweg announced that the 501c nonprofit will move WordCamps to its own company, WordPress Community Support, forming a PBC (Public Benefit Corporation) that is fully owned by the Foundation.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;He explained that if certain things happened at WordCamps it could endanger the overall Foundation, so WordCamps will now be managed under their own entity where the events will have a little more flexibility in how they do things. The Foundation plans to support some like-minded nonprofits that are aligned with the overall education mission of the organization, including &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.hackthehood.org/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Hack the Hood&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://archive.org/index.php&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Internet Archive&lt;/a&gt;, and &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.blackgirlscode.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Black Girls Code&lt;/a&gt;. In 2017 the Foundation will also begin promoting hackathons to help nonprofits and NGO&amp;#8217;s.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot;&gt;&lt;p lang=&quot;en&quot; dir=&quot;ltr&quot;&gt;The Foundation will focus on supporting like-minded non-profits, education/workshops, and hackathons that benefit non-profits/NGOs. &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/hashtag/wcus?src=hash&quot;&gt;#wcus&lt;/a&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;https://t.co/6VfdP82KuM&quot;&gt;pic.twitter.com/6VfdP82KuM&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;mdash; WordCamp US (@WordCampUS) &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/WordCampUS/status/805158678353608704&quot;&gt;December 3, 2016&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Internationalization is Driving an Increase in Plugin Usage&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Mullenweg shared a few stats about the plugin directory, which will soon be launching a new design with revamped search functionality. This year has seen a 20% increase in active plugin usage and a 34% increase in plugin downloads totaling 1.48 billion, which Mullenweg attributed to a spike in internationalization efforts over the past year. The number of translation contributors has grown from 5,000 in April 2015 to 17,000 as of November 2016.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This year there were 1,598 plugins with language packs (up from 314 last year) and 1224 themes with language packs (up from 641 last year). Mullenweg noted that 2/3 of the world speaks one of 12 languages with native fluency and that WordPress covers all of these and many more. In fact, the 4.6 release shipped with support for 50 available languages. WordPress&amp;#8217; top 10 plugins are now 82% complete in the top 12 languages.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot;&gt;&lt;p lang=&quot;en&quot; dir=&quot;ltr&quot;&gt;The top 10 plugins are 82% complete in the top 12 languages. &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/hashtag/wcus?src=hash&quot;&gt;#wcus&lt;/a&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;https://t.co/LnpEGv0p7o&quot;&gt;pic.twitter.com/LnpEGv0p7o&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;mdash; WordCamp US (@WordCampUS) &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/WordCampUS/status/805161007349985280&quot;&gt;December 3, 2016&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Mullenweg Continues to Push Calypso as the Future of the WordPress Interface&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;During the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wptavern.com/state-of-the-word-2015-javascript-and-api-driven-interfaces-are-the-future-of-wordpress&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;2015 State of the Word&lt;/a&gt;, Mullenweg gave attendees a homework assignment to &amp;#8220;learn JavaScript deeply&amp;#8221; and &lt;a href=&quot;https://youtu.be/TX6dXRL-jPU?t=59m14s&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;promised to submit a JavaScript patch before 4.7&lt;/a&gt; came out. He submitted his first pull request to Calypso yesterday, Automattic&amp;#8217;s from-scratch rewrite of WP admin using Node and React.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress.com users have widely adopted the new interface for publishing. Mullenweg shared statistics showing that 68% of posts went through Calypso since its launch, 17% via mobile, and 15% through the traditional wp-admin. Mobile app and mobile browser usage are also up. &amp;#8220;We now need to start thinking about mobile devices as the primary way people are going to interact with WordPress in the future,&amp;#8221; Mullenweg said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;From the time it launched, Mullenweg has said that Calypso, or something like it, would be the future of the WordPress interface. He reiterated this in his 2016 address and has committed some of Automattic&amp;#8217;s JavaScript developers from the Calypso team to contribute full-time to core.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If Calypso has a chance at becoming a promising replacement for the WordPress admin, its creators will need to broaden its interoperability with the WordPress plugin ecosystem. Mullenweg announced that Calypso is now plugin aware and is open to plugins with over 1M active sites.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The next step on Calypso&amp;#8217;s roadmap is to bring in support for Automattic&amp;#8217;s plugins &amp;#8211; WooCommerce, Akismet, Jetpack, and VaultPress. Mullenweg said the big focus for 2017 is to make plugins Calypso-aware, starting with a handful of the most popular ones before opening it up to all plugins.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;The hope is that Calypso, or something like it, is actually what becomes the interface that drives WordPress,&amp;#8221; Mullenweg said. Since no one is currently building anything like Calypso and targeting core, it looks like the technology behind WordPress.com will be driving the evolution of WordPress in 2017.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If Mullenweg&amp;#8217;s goal is to make Calypso the primary publishing engine for core WordPress, one of the major challenges will be getting plugin developers on board with building compatibility for what is currently an Automattic product. What are the implications of contributing to greater Calypso adoption? If core brings in the Calypso interface in the future, would Automattic push to include its Reader and other WordPress.com functionality, as it has in the mobile apps? These are questions developers will need to weigh when considering whether to pursue a more application-type experience via the Calypso interface.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot;&gt;&lt;p lang=&quot;en&quot; dir=&quot;ltr&quot;&gt;What's next for Calypso? We'll start bringing &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/automattic&quot;&gt;@Automattic&lt;/a&gt;'s plugins in. &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/hashtag/wcus?src=hash&quot;&gt;#wcus&lt;/a&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;https://t.co/RL8ZduRczM&quot;&gt;pic.twitter.com/RL8ZduRczM&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;mdash; WordCamp US (@WordCampUS) &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/WordCampUS/status/805165388006887424&quot;&gt;December 3, 2016&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;WordPress Recommends Hosts Offering PHP 7+ and HTTPS by Default&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress core continues to update its recommendations and requirements with the help of hosts who are adopting the latest technologies. The &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/about/requirements/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;official recommendation for WordPress hosting&lt;/a&gt; is now PHP 7 or higher. After WordPress.com switched to be 100% on PHP 7, Mullenweg said the network&amp;#8217;s performance doubled and CPU load fell in half. Just 4% of self-hosted sites are on PHP 7, but the new recommendation should help move more hosts towards getting their customers updated.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot;&gt;&lt;p lang=&quot;en&quot; dir=&quot;ltr&quot;&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://t.co/VrQffeOtG0&quot;&gt;https://t.co/VrQffeOtG0&lt;/a&gt; has been 100% switched over to PHP7, bringing significant performance improvements. &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/hashtag/wcus?src=hash&quot;&gt;#wcus&lt;/a&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;https://t.co/MChiS9QBJh&quot;&gt;pic.twitter.com/MChiS9QBJh&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;mdash; WordCamp US (@WordCampUS) &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/WordCampUS/status/805164029371158528&quot;&gt;December 3, 2016&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Beginning in 2017, WordPress will have progressive enhancement for certain features that are only available for encrypted sites. Mullenweg announced that WordPress.org is now tracking HTTPS adoption. So far 11.45% of active WordPress websites are on HTTPS and &lt;a href=&quot;https://wptavern.com/wordpress-will-only-recommend-hosting-companies-offering-ssl-by-default-in-2017&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;the project will no longer recommend hosts that do not offer it by default&lt;/a&gt;. &amp;#8220;We want to bring more of the web to be secure, which is especially important in the post-Snowden era,&amp;#8221; he said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Trying New Things: Major Changes Coming to WordPress&amp;#8217; Core Release Cycle&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.7 release lead Helen Hou-Sandí joined Mullenweg on stage to highlight a few of the features and improvements that will be coming in the official release on Tuesday. The release is arguably one of the most exciting and successful updates for WordPress in some time, but Mullenweg has a new strategy for core development in 2017.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;We&amp;#8217;re at a junction for WordPress where what got us here wont get us there,&amp;#8221; Mullenweg said, after highlighting how the software&amp;#8217;s market share has grown from 13.1% to 27.2% in the past five years.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Mullenweg proposed a new structure for WordPress releases where design and user testing will lead the way. &amp;#8220;I&amp;#8217;m putting back on the &amp;#8216;product lead&amp;#8217; hat for 2017,&amp;#8221; he said. The upcoming year will have no set release schedule. Mullenweg is upending WordPress&amp;#8217; predictable release cycle in favor of tackling some larger items on the to-do list. He said the focus will be on performance and fixes to existing functionality in three main focus areas: WP REST API, the Editor, and the Customizer.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Mullenweg said he is particularly interested in getting first-party usage of the REST API in the admin, in hopes of having it evolve to something the project can use for the next decade. If it doesn&amp;#8217;t, he said core will consider bringing it back into a plugin specifically for developers.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Mullenweg said he feels the editor does not represent the core of WordPress publishing, a sentiment that many users agree with. He hopes to steer it toward a more block-based approach that unifies widgets and includes an interface for shortcodes.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Mullenweg&amp;#8217;s vision for the Customizer is to see all aspects of WordPress become more instant and provide the same interface and UI affordances as the editor. He announced that Ephox, the company behind TinyMCE, has agreed to work with the project to improve the core editing experience.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Shifting from a time-based release cycle to one that is more project-based is a major departure from WordPress&amp;#8217; previous release philosophy of &amp;#8220;Deadlines are not arbitrary.&amp;#8221; The project&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/about/philosophy/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;philosophy page&lt;/a&gt; identifies the practice of delaying releases for one more feature as a &amp;#8220;rabbit hole&amp;#8221; that has been tested and found to be unpleasant. The new approach to core development makes no guarantee that WordPress will have any releases in 2017.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If the experiment is not a success, the project&amp;#8217;s days of frequent and fast iteration may be over for awhile. Mullenweg is willing to risk it in hopes of being able to provide more product-based leadership that will distinguish WordPress from its proprietary competitors.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot;&gt;&lt;p lang=&quot;en&quot; dir=&quot;ltr&quot;&gt;Words of wisdom from &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/kristatippett&quot;&gt;@kristatippett&lt;/a&gt;: &quot;We only learn to walk when we risk falling down&amp;#8211;&quot; &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/hashtag/wcus?src=hash&quot;&gt;#wcus&lt;/a&gt; &lt;a href=&quot;https://t.co/6t5sD6Xjbm&quot;&gt;pic.twitter.com/6t5sD6Xjbm&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;mdash; WordCamp US (@WordCampUS) &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/WordCampUS/status/805170327726780416&quot;&gt;December 3, 2016&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
