&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;I think we&amp;#8217;re trying to counter stagnation,&amp;#8221; Mullenweg said when asked about the new approach to releases in the Q&amp;amp;A segment. &amp;#8220;Even though we&amp;#8217;ve had lots of releases, certain parts of WordPress have stagnated and haven&amp;#8217;t made the leaps that they could.&amp;#8221;  He suggested that being part of a feature plugin team will give developers a way to be involved in more active releases and continue to build momentum for eventual inclusion of their projects in core.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Mullenweg plans to identify a tech lead and a design lead and will be working with them as the overall product lead. He envisions that when one area of WordPress gets to the point where the software can ship significant user-facing improvements, a release will be born.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;We&amp;#8217;re at the point now where the steps WordPress needs to take are more significant to get the other 73% of the web it doesn&amp;#8217;t have yet,&amp;#8221; Mullenweg said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In a return to WordPress&amp;#8217; poetic roots, he concluded by reading a poem called &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.poets.org/poetsorg/poem/praise-song-day&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Praise Song&lt;/a&gt; for the Day by Elizabeth Alexander.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The video of the State of the Word address will soon be available on &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCpJf6LGZ0a4n9Lj4aVt9spg&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WordPress&amp;#8217; new YouTube channel&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;epoch-width-sniffer&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Sun, 04 Dec 2016 18:50:17 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:1;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:51:&quot;Post Status: Matt Mullenweg State of the Word, 2016&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;https://poststatus.com/?p=30865&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:54:&quot;https://poststatus.com/matt-mullenweg-state-word-2016/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:16572:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Matt Mullenweg just completed the 2016 State of the Word presentation at WordCamp US 2016.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This year, Matt focused on a variety of important topics, including the state of user experience in WordPress today, goals for future interface improvements, a WordPress growth council, internationalization gains, the further proliferation of secure websites, and important changes to the WordPress development process.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;WordCamp US in Philadelphia&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt began his talk by thanking the city of Philadelphia for being a great host of the first two WordCamp US events, as well as the sponsors, organizers, and volunteers that helped make WordCamp US one of the most successful and smoothest run WordCamps ever.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;He also said the per person cost for WordCamp US is over $500 per person, and that only the sponsors make that happen. And next year, WordCamp US is making its way to Nashville.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;WordCamps and meetups in 2016&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;There were 116 WordCamps in 2016, and over 36,000 attendees, 2,056 speakers, 1,036 sponsors, and 750 organizers.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;There were 3,193 meetup events in 58 countries. These were attended by more than 62,000 people, or nearly double WordCamps.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt says it&amp;#8217;s the fastest growth there has been for these events in around five or six years. WordCamp Europe actually had more people than WordCamp US this year, which Matt took as a personal challenge for Nashville.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress.tv publishes more than 26% of all talks, and now there is an official WordPress channel on YouTube, so more and more videos will begin to be available wherever people want to watch them.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;WordCamp public benefit corporation&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;More than a year ago, work began to separate WordCamps from the WordPress Foundation, in order to make WordPress event organizing more flexible and to better protect the WordPress trademarks that the foundation holds.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;One of the things the new public benefit corporation will be able to do is support like minded non-profits, and in 2017 will be sponsoring three: Hack the Hood, the Internet Archive, and Black Girls Code.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Also, the organization will start to promote hackathons for non-profits and NGOs.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;WordPress&amp;#8217;s extended family&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt gave a shoutout to WordPress&amp;#8217;s &amp;#8220;cousins&amp;#8221; like BuddyPress and bbPress, highlighting a lot of features that have gone into the software in the last year.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;BuddyPress and bbPress&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress.org itself uses BuddyPress and bbPress. For ages, it&amp;#8217;s used outdated versions of bbPress, and in the past year launched a new support form that uses modern bbPress and WordPress profiles use bbPress. Matt says projects like these will get new support and engagement over the next year.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;HackerOne&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;HackerOne is a security website that allows software organizations to offer bounties to hackers for responsibly disclosing security bugs.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;GlotPress&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;GlotPress has had a big transformation in the last year, as it is no longer standalone software on top of BackPress, but rather a plugin for WordPress. If you&amp;#8217;ve never been to &lt;a href=&quot;https://translate.wordpress.org/&quot;&gt;translate.WordPress.org&lt;/a&gt;, you&amp;#8217;ve seen GlotPress in action, and it&amp;#8217;s pretty amazing.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;WordPress.org&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org&quot;&gt;WordPress.org&lt;/a&gt; is a central hub for the WordPress community. Matt highlighted some of the work that&amp;#8217;s been going on this past year around languages, support forums, and more. He also says that new work will be going into P2/O2, which are used for the &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org&quot;&gt;Make WordPress&lt;/a&gt; blogs.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;And he gave attention to the new WordPress plugin repository, which finally uses WordPress itself, and has a whole new design. You can see the new design in action on the new &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/plugins-wp/&quot;&gt;demo site&lt;/a&gt;, which should role out to the main Plugins directory soon.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;WordPress in all languages&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.6 was available in 50 languages the day it was released. And the top 10 plugins are 82% translated in the top 12 languages used in WordPress.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Language packs have been a huge help in helping translate plugins as a community project on Translate.WordPress.org, rather than having to ship translations inside the plugin itself.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;1,598 plugins are now using language packs, and 1,224 themes use them. This is huge for the future of WordPress working great in every language.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Also, in WordPress 4.7, we&amp;#8217;ll see per-user language choices.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Learning JavaScript Deeply&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Last year&amp;#8217;s homework for the community was to learn JavaScript deeply. He says that WordPress is 28% JavaScript now, which hasn&amp;#8217;t changed, but he says we&amp;#8217;ve still made a lot of progress.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt gave himself a personal challenge to learn JavaScript, and he said that 364 days into this challenge, he submitted his first patch to Calypso (Automattic&amp;#8217;s WordPress administration interface). He said, learning JavaScript and becoming as native with JavaScript as with PHP is going to be really important &amp;#8212; especially as the REST API gets included in WordPress 4.7.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;WordPress Growth Council&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt recently posted about a WordPress Growth Council to help WordPress grow and maintain marketshare.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;He says that what got WordPress to where it is today, won&amp;#8217;t get WordPress to where it can be tomorrow. He blogged about this &lt;a href=&quot;https://ma.tt/2016/12/wp-growth-council/&quot;&gt;new growth council&lt;/a&gt;, which folks can apply for, which will help guide product direction in WordPress going forward.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt actually said in Post Status Slack recently that if WordPress doesn&amp;#8217;t make changes to the interface and otherwise, he&amp;#8217;d expect WordPress marketshare would begin to decline by 2018.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;HTTPS &amp;amp; PHP7&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;11.45% of WordPress websites are now served via HTTPS. Matt talked last year about how LetsEncrypt and PHP7 were going to be a big deal, but they&amp;#8217;ve turned out to be, &amp;#8220;huge.&amp;#8221; And WordPress will now start applying progressive enhancement techniques for WordPress websites.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress.com is now fully on PHP7, which he says was an enormous accomplishment. He&amp;#8217;s also announced that &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/about/requirements/&quot;&gt;WordPress.org will now recommend&lt;/a&gt; PHP7 by default.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Calypso&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt gave some updates on &lt;a href=&quot;https://developer.wordpress.com/calypso/&quot;&gt;Calypso&amp;#8217;s&lt;/a&gt; adoption since it was released last year. He says that 68% of posts on WordPress.com are now written in Calypso. 17% of posts are written via a mobile device, and only 15% of users are using the WordPress admin. For reference, Calypso is the default method of publishing on WordPress.com now, so that includes the desktop website, desktop app, and mobile app.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt says that building Calypso is like, &amp;#8220;building a plane while it&amp;#8217;s flying.&amp;#8221; And while it&amp;#8217;s hard, he says it&amp;#8217;s worth it, but it&amp;#8217;s like rebuilding WordPress &amp;#8212; which took 13 years to do &amp;#8212; in only two years.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The future of Calypso includes making it &amp;#8220;plugin aware&amp;#8221;, so that prominent plugins (most Automattic plugins included) would be recognized and manageable via Calypso.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In fact, Calypso is plugin aware today, as the merge has just happened. So now plugins can include custom code to be manageable via Calypso. This is an interesting move to me, especially since Calypso &amp;#8212; while open source &amp;#8212; isn&amp;#8217;t an official WordPress project, but rather an Automattic-owned interface.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt says that someday he&amp;#8217;s like to see Calypso, &amp;#8220;or something like it,&amp;#8221; eventually to become the WordPress interface.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Core releases in 2016&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.5-4.7 will have been released by the end of 2016. Matt says, &amp;#8220;this is very much a year about doing things differently.&amp;#8221; And in that spirit, he&amp;#8217;s pre-announcing the jazz musician in the release. I&amp;#8217;m sure Jeffro will be pleased &lt;img src=&quot;https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/72x72/1f609.png&quot; alt=&quot;?&quot; class=&quot;wp-smiley&quot; /&gt; WordPress 4.7 will be named &amp;#8220;Vaughan&amp;#8221;, after jazz musician Sarah &amp;#8220;Sassy&amp;#8221; Vaughan.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Helen Hou-Sandi came to the stage to discuss WordPress 4.7 in more detail.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;WordPress 4.7&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.7 will include a variety of features, and will be released on Tuesday, December 6th.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;New default theme&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress includes a new default theme that with a multi-section home page that&amp;#8217;s a brand new WordPress feature. And generally Twenty Seventeen has a lot more broad base appeal for businesses and non-blogging applications than many past themes.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Theme setup process&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Helen really wanted to focus on user interactions in WordPress 4.7. She used the example of her &amp;#8220;tweet storm&amp;#8221; about what it&amp;#8217;s like to change a theme, which took dozens of steps and included a lot of unclear processes.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Themes in 4.7 can define content that ships with the theme, such as a nav menu setup, sample page content, a password protected page, and other content that would be utilized in the theme. This will be a massive improvement in the initial theme setup experience that I love to see in 4.7.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Better menu handling&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.7 includes better menu building that will also assist the new user experience. Now when you are building a menu in the customizer, you can add a page right from the menu screen, so that if you haven&amp;#8217;t yet written your &amp;#8220;about&amp;#8221; page or whatever else, you&amp;#8217;ll be able to create that draft straight from the menu screen, so the user doesn&amp;#8217;t have to know exactly which flow is necessary to setup their site.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;&amp;#8220;Sleeper hits&amp;#8221;&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Helen highlights sleeper features, like thumbnail previews for PDFs and user dashboard languages so a user can use a different language than is set by the site administrator.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;The WordPress REST API&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;To big applause, Helen noted the inclusion of the WordPress REST API Content Endpoints in 4.7. She says that she&amp;#8217;s excited to take the momentum and excitement around the API and turn it into more real-world projects where people test and put it to practice.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Deputy leads&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Jeff Paul and Aaron Jorbin were the deputy release leads for 4.7, and more than 475 contributors submitted code to 4.7. Over 200 of those contributors are first time contributors.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Sneak preview video&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;To end the preview of WordPress 4.7, Helen shared a sneak preview of the WordPress 4.7 video, created by friend Rami Abraham, that highlights &amp;#8220;Carly&amp;#8221;, who is a small business owner building her business website. The video shows a couple more great sleeper hits, like customizer preview icons to help editing, and video headers.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;That&amp;#8217;s WordPress 4.7&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.7, I believe, is going to be one of the best releases we&amp;#8217;ve seen in a long, long time. It&amp;#8217;s jam packed, and while I&amp;#8217;m sure we&amp;#8217;ll have plenty of follow-on work, there&amp;#8217;s been a hugely ambitious effort with tons of awesome contributors. None of it would&amp;#8217;ve happened without Helen.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;WordPress REST API and examples&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;After the video, Matt came back on stage.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt highlighted some of the REST API examples, including the new &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.guggenheim.org/&quot;&gt;Guggenheim Museum&lt;/a&gt; website and &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.vocativ.com/&quot;&gt;Vocativ&lt;/a&gt;, which both use the new API, and are powered by Content Endpoints.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;A look at the past and future&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt spent a few minutes reflecting over this past, and busy, year; but also spent time discussing the past few years and what&amp;#8217;s in store in the future.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt recognized the &amp;#8220;predictable&amp;#8221; release cycle that we moved to around WordPress 3.8, and how that&amp;#8217;s been a huge benefit for the platform in general.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In the past five years, we&amp;#8217;ve seen WordPress go from 13.1% to 27.2%, and this kind of marketshare for a CMS is &amp;#8220;unprecedented.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;He says, &amp;#8220;What can we try next?&amp;#8221; In other words, he wants to do things differently going forward: &amp;#8220;What got us here, won&amp;#8217;t get us there.&amp;#8221; In order to do this, he&amp;#8217;s proposing a new structure for core development.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt said he wants to see a simpler, faster UX, while simultaneously making it more powerful. This has been my number one goal for WordPress the last few years, so I&amp;#8217;m thrilled to see him highlight it. In the coming releases, he, &amp;#8220;wants to see design leading the way.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In 2017, Matt says he&amp;#8217;s going to be a heavily involved project lead again.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;No set major releases in 2017&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt made a huge announcement by saying that there will be no set releases in 2017. WordPress Core will continue to move forward, managing maintenance and other items, but will shift to three main focuses for features that will dictate the next several major releases:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Number 1) The WordPress REST API&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;He says we need shift from thinking about the input, to measuring the output. He wants the conversation of success metrics to get beyond the &amp;#8220;thousands&amp;#8221; when, &amp;#8220;WordPress is in the tens of millions.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt sees powering the WordPress admin with the REST API as a core focus for 2017. In addition, this effort will include shipping authentication tools in WordPress core, so that external applications can connect to WordPress websites. He says if we can&amp;#8217;t move forward with this goal, then we need to consider making the API a plugin again.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Number 2) The Editor&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt wants to see a lot of work on the WordPress editing experience. Matt says he showed &amp;#8220;block-faced editor&amp;#8221; in a State of the Word slide a few years ago, and calls it his &amp;#8220;white whale&amp;#8221;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;He says we need to be candid about our shortcomings with WordPress so that we can more effectively move forward. Andrew Ozz and Ella Van Isuelde have been massively influential on the editor improvements we&amp;#8217;ve seen over the past few years, and their contributions will be huge for moving this goal forward.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Number 3) The Customizer&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;The customizer is not yet fast enough, and flexible enough, to meet our current needs.&amp;#8221; He&amp;#8217;s excited to see all the new work going into the customizer, but knows there&amp;#8217;s a lot of work to do to take the customizer to the next step.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;How to get these goals accomplished&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;He says that new major versions of WordPress will not be released until these features are ready. He says that as each project is completed, there will be a major release to go around it.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I&amp;#8217;m fascinated by this new approach. It&amp;#8217;s like taking the current feature project framework and taking it multiple levels up. It&amp;#8217;s definitely a way to shake things up, and that may be great, considering so many people in the WordPress space enjoy complaining about the slow process that is WordPress feature development.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt, as project lead, says he&amp;#8217;ll personally be taking these on as the lead. And work will begin immediately to make it happen.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;So, I don&amp;#8217;t know if the next release will be called WordPress 4.8, or when it will be, but I&amp;#8217;d be shocked if it&amp;#8217;s four months like past releases. But I guess we&amp;#8217;ll see a lot of minor releases for all the other aspects of core development.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt says he thinks we&amp;#8217;ll fall while we learn to walk in this new way, and that&amp;#8217;s okay.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;hr /&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I have to admit, these are some pretty surprising announcements. I&amp;#8217;m excited to dig more into the particulars over the coming weeks, but I do think this serves as a worthwhile and important jolt into WordPress core development. That&amp;#8217;s not to say I think WordPress development has been bad, I think it&amp;#8217;s been great.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Matt finished by reading a poem by Elizabeth Alexander, titled, &amp;#8220;&lt;a href=&quot;https://www.poetryfoundation.org/poems-and-poets/poems/detail/52141&quot;&gt;Praise Song For The Day&lt;/a&gt;&amp;#8221; that marked a fitting end to the talk.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I think the key takeaway should be like he said: &amp;#8220;what got us here, won&amp;#8217;t get us there.&amp;#8221; Let&amp;#8217;s see how this goes.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Photo credit: Brian Richards for Post Status.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Sat, 03 Dec 2016 22:20:17 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:15:&quot;Brian Krogsgard&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:2;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:26:&quot;Matt: WordCamp Live Stream&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:22:&quot;https://ma.tt/?p=46945&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:43:&quot;https://ma.tt/2016/12/wordcamp-live-stream/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:298:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Later today (3:45pm ET) I&amp;#8217;ll deliver my annual State of the Word speech, which I&amp;#8217;m very excited about. If you&amp;#8217;d like to watch remotely, this year live stream tickets are &lt;strong&gt;free&lt;/strong&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;https://2016.us.wordcamp.org/live-stream/&quot;&gt;you can tune in here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Sat, 03 Dec 2016 11:54:15 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4:&quot;Matt&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:3;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:72:&quot;WPTavern: DigitalCube Launches Shifter, Serverless Hosting for WordPress&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:29:&quot;https://wptavern.com/?p=64157&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:82:&quot;https://wptavern.com/digitalcube-launches-shifter-serverless-hosting-for-wordpress&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3811:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/shifter-logo.png?ssl=1&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;https://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/shifter-logo.png?resize=1025%2C419&amp;ssl=1&quot; alt=&quot;shifter-logo&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-64169&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://en.digitalcube.jp/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;DigitalCube&lt;/a&gt; launched &lt;a href=&quot;https://getshifter.io/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Shifter&lt;/a&gt; at WordCamp US today, the first serverless hosting product for WordPress. The Japanese development company specializes in WordPress and AWS integrations. Shifter was built by the same team behind the company&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;https://amimoto-ami.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Amimoto&lt;/a&gt; cloud hosting platform.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Shifter converts WordPress sites into a series of static HTML files and serves them up via a global CDN (AWS) for high performance hosting, eliminating the burden of software maintenance and server updates. The product targets websites that have a low frequency of updates, such as business or portfolio sites, as well as maintenance and support providers.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Shifter allows site owners to turn WordPress on or off in its administration center. The service is a hybrid of a WordPress static site generator and a hosting solution. Shifter hosts the static files it creates and allows users to connect their domains. It leaves the standard WordPress management and administration workflow intact and compiles a new version of the static files anytime users update content inside WordPress. The service starts at $30/month and offers support for unlimited sites.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;https://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/shifter-dashboard.png?ssl=1&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;https://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/shifter-dashboard.png?resize=1025%2C652&amp;ssl=1&quot; alt=&quot;Shifter dashboard&quot; class=&quot;size-full wp-image-64166&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Shifter dashboard
&lt;p&gt;As the first commercial product to provide serverless WordPress hosting, Shifter offers a unique way to tackle the security concerns that plague WordPress and its plugins and themes. Because the software is used by more than 27% of all websites, it has become a big target for hackers and spammers alike. Shifter&amp;#8217;s creators see WordPress as a prime candidate for serverless architecture.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;DigitalCube team members met the Philadelphia-based &lt;a href=&quot;http://j2made.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;J2 Design&lt;/a&gt; company at last year&amp;#8217;s WordCamp US and partnered with them to improve their branding, copy writing, and approach.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;At that time, we were having problems in design, branding, and communication,&amp;#8221; product liaison Shinichi Nishikawa said. &amp;#8220;The name &amp;#8216;Amimoto&amp;#8217; was originally a Japanese word and was difficult for people to pronounce or remember. We saw their work and asked them if we could form a partnership.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Together the Amimoto and J2 Design teams took the project from concept to launch in about three months. They built Shifter with AWS, Docker, and the Serverless Framework. The development team behind the project also supports and manages sites such as The Japan Times, AOL Japan, and Mazda. They frequently contribute to open source projects, including WordPress, Serverless Framework, and WP-CLI.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Shifter has exited beta and the company has &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.kickstarter.com/projects/225627578/shifter-serverless-hosting-for-wordpress&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;launched a Kickstarter campaign&lt;/a&gt; with a $10,000 goal to fund future development on the project&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;https://getshifter.io/blog/development-roadmap/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;roadmap&lt;/a&gt;, including domain mapping, a way to visualize usage of bandwidth and storage, multi-factor authentication, advanced scheduling, and WP-CLI support.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;epoch-width-sniffer&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Sat, 03 Dec 2016 03:44:56 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:4;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:23:&quot;Matt: WP Growth Council&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:22:&quot;https://ma.tt/?p=46933&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:40:&quot;https://ma.tt/2016/12/wp-growth-council/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1594:&quot;&lt;p&gt;In the WordPress world, when we look back an 2016 I think we&amp;#8217;ll remember it as the year that we awoke to the importance of marketing. WordPress has always grown organically through word of mouth and its passionate community, but the hundreds of millions being spent advertising against WP has started to have an impact, especially for folks only lightly familiar with us.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I&amp;#8217;ve started to hear about a number of folks across many WordPress companies and industries working on this from different angles, some approaching it from an enterprise point of view and some from a consumer point of view. There&amp;#8217;s an opportunity for learning from each other, almost like a mastermind group. As the survey says:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Never have there been more threats to the open web and WordPress. Over three hundred million dollars has been spent in 2016 advertising proprietary systems, and even more is happening in investment. No one company in the WP world is large enough to fight this, nor should anyone need to do it on their own. We&amp;#8217;d like to bring together organizations that would like to contribute to growing WordPress. It will be a small group, and if you or your organization are interested in being a part please fill out the survey below.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;By working together we can amplify our efforts to bring open source to a wider audience, and fulfill WordPress&amp;#8217; mission to truly democratize publishing.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If this sounds interesting to you, &lt;a href=&quot;http://mcm.polldaddy.com/s/wordpress-growth-council&quot;&gt;apply using this survey&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Fri, 02 Dec 2016 16:22:51 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4:&quot;Matt&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:5;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:89:&quot;WPTavern: WordPress Will Only Recommend Hosting Companies Offering SSL by Default in 2017&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:29:&quot;https://wptavern.com/?p=64081&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:100:&quot;https://wptavern.com/wordpress-will-only-recommend-hosting-companies-offering-ssl-by-default-in-2017&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3276:&quot;&lt;p&gt;In October, &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/letsencrypt/status/788449815986262016&quot;&gt;Let&amp;#8217;s Encrypt&lt;/a&gt; was managing more than 10 million active SSL certificates. That &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/letsencrypt/status/802972766525865984&quot;&gt;number doubled to 20 million&lt;/a&gt; in November as large  providers continue to partner with the organization to manage their customers&amp;#8217; certificates.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In 2014, Google announced that HTTPS &lt;a href=&quot;https://security.googleblog.com/2014/08/https-as-ranking-signal_6.html&quot;&gt;is a ranking factor&lt;/a&gt;. Earlier this year, the Google Chrome security team &lt;a href=&quot;https://wptavern.com/chrome-to-add-security-warning-to-http-sites-beginning-2017&quot;&gt;announced&lt;/a&gt; that Chrome 56 will mark HTTP sites that transmit passwords or credit cards as insecure.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;aligncenter wp-image-60902 size-full&quot; src=&quot;https://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/09/chrome-http-warning.png?resize=640%2C251&amp;ssl=1&quot; alt=&quot;chrome-http-warning&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In 2017, managed WordPress hosting companies will have one more reason to enable SSL by default for new accounts. In a &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/12/moving-toward-ssl/&quot;&gt;post on the WordPress.org blog&lt;/a&gt;, Matt Mullenweg, co-founder of the open source WordPress project, explains what the project is going to do to encourage HTTPS by default across the web.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Early in 2017, we will only promote hosting partners that provide a SSL certificate by default in their accounts,&amp;#8221; Mullenweg said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Later we will begin to assess which features, such as API authentication, would benefit the most from SSL and make them only enabled when SSL is there.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Unrelated to SSL, Mullenweg also commented on the significant performance improvements in PHP7 and will consider whether hosting partners use PHP7 by default for new accounts in 2017.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;These moves are a continued effort by Mullenweg to secure and encrypt as much of the web as possible. Earlier this year, WordPress.com &lt;a href=&quot;https://en.blog.wordpress.com/2016/04/08/https-everywhere-encryption-for-all-wordpress-com-sites/&quot;&gt;encrypted all of its sites&lt;/a&gt; using Let&amp;#8217;s Encrypt.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://letsencrypt.org/&quot;&gt;Let&amp;#8217;s Encrypt&lt;/a&gt; is an initiative which aims to encrypt 100% of the web by making trusted certificates available to everyone at no cost. It&amp;#8217;s a 501(c)(3) nonprofit and recently launched a &lt;a href=&quot;https://letsencrypt.org/2016/11/01/launching-our-crowdfunding-campaign.html&quot;&gt;crowdfunding campaign&lt;/a&gt; to cover the cost of one month of operations totaling $200K.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Josh Aas, ISRG Executive Director, explains the reasons behind the crowdfunding campaign, &amp;#8220;First, there is a gap between the funds we’ve raised and what we need for next year,&amp;#8221; Aas said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Second, we believe individual supporters from our community can come to represent a significant diversification of our annual revenue sources, in addition to corporate sponsorship and grants.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;To learn more about the campaign and to contribute, visit &lt;a href=&quot;https://letsencrypt.org/2016/11/01/launching-our-crowdfunding-campaign.html&quot;&gt;Let&amp;#8217;s Encrypt&amp;#8217;s Indiegogo&lt;/a&gt; page.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;epoch-width-sniffer&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 01 Dec 2016 21:10:54 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:6;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:27:&quot;Dev Blog: Moving Toward SSL&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:34:&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/?p=4588&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:53:&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/12/moving-toward-ssl/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1626:&quot;&lt;p&gt;We’re at a turning point: 2017 is going to be the year that we’re going to see features in WordPress which require hosts to have HTTPS available. Just as JavaScript is a near necessity for smoother user experiences and more modern PHP versions are critical for performance, SSL just makes sense as the next hurdle our users are going to face.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;SSL basically means the link between your browser and the server is encrypted. SSL used to be difficult to implement, and often expensive or slow. Modern browsers, and the incredible success of projects like &lt;a href=&quot;https://letsencrypt.org/&quot;&gt;Let&amp;#8217;s Encrypt&lt;/a&gt; have made getting a certificate to secure your site fast, free, and something we think every host should support by default, especially in a post-Snowden era. Google also weighs &lt;a href=&quot;https://security.googleblog.com/2014/08/https-as-ranking-signal_6.html&quot;&gt;SSL as a search engine ranking factor&lt;/a&gt; and will begin &lt;a href=&quot;http://motherboard.vice.com/read/google-will-soon-shame-all-websites-that-are-unencrypted-chrome-https&quot;&gt;flagging unencrypted sites in Chrome&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;First, early in 2017, we will only promote hosting partners that provide a SSL certificate by default in their accounts. Later we will begin to assess which features, such as API authentication, would benefit the most from SSL and make them only enabled when SSL is there.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Separately, I also think the performance improvements in PHP7 are particularly impressive, and major kudos to everyone who worked on that. We will consider whether hosts use PHP7 by default for new accounts next year as well.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 01 Dec 2016 17:20:29 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:14:&quot;Matt Mullenweg&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:7;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:71:&quot;WPTavern: Flywheel Acquires WordPress Local Development Tool Pressmatic&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:29:&quot;https://wptavern.com/?p=64057&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:82:&quot;https://wptavern.com/flywheel-acquires-wordpress-local-development-tool-pressmatic&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3671:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Flywheel has acquired Pressmatic, a local WordPress development application for OS X. The application was created by &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/claygriffiths&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Clay Griffiths&lt;/a&gt;, who will be joining Flywheel to support the product as part of the acquisition.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://pressmatic.io/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Pressmatic&lt;/a&gt; launched in July 2016 with a $129 price tag but Flywheel is opening it up for free for all users. The company is rebranding the product as &amp;#8220;Local by Flywheel&amp;#8221; and plans to create a Windows application, add off-site backups for local sites, and sell premium support.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;“From the start, the application encompassed so many of Flywheel’s core values: speed, simplicity, and allowing designers and developers the freedom to do what they love,&amp;#8221; Flywheel CEO and co-founder Dusty Davidson said. &amp;#8220;It’s a perfect fit.”&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Griffiths told the Tavern that he is excited for the opportunities that Flywheel can provide for Local going forward. &amp;#8220;I originally built Pressmatic because I saw the gap that existed for a truly great local WordPress development experience, and now with the resources and team at Flywheel we&amp;#8217;re set to really build something great,&amp;#8221; Griffiths said. &amp;#8220;I certainly could have continued to go at it alone, but after meeting the team it became clear that the right answer was to partner up and really go big.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Griffiths Plans to Continue Headway Themes Support and Development in his Spare Time&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The acquisition comes just months after Griffiths, who is also the co-founder of Headway Themes, was embroiled in the controversy surrounding the company&amp;#8217;s lack of communication and decline in support. Many potential customers were turned off to Pressmatic as the result of Griffith&amp;#8217;s lack of support for Headway Themes&amp;#8217; customers and its mistreatment of employees. They company publicly confirmed its financial troubles and &lt;a href=&quot;https://wptavern.com/headway-themes-confirms-financial-difficulties-issues-apology-to-customers&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;apologized to customers&lt;/a&gt; after &lt;a href=&quot;https://wptavern.com/former-headway-themes-employee-goes-public-staff-has-not-been-paid-and-customers-are-not-receiving-support&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;a former employee went public&lt;/a&gt; about not having been paid and customers not receiving support.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;When asked how the Pressmattic acquisition affects Headway Themes customers, Griffiths confirmed that he will continue to be involved with support and development of Headway.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;This acquisition and employment will provide myself and my family much more stability than we&amp;#8217;ve had in a long time, and will allow me to better focus on Headway in my spare time,&amp;#8221; Griffiths said. &amp;#8220;This includes rolling out the upcoming 4.1 release, and working hard to make sure the support and other outstanding issues are resolved for all our customers.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Pressmatic is used by hundreds of WordPress developers and is Flywheel&amp;#8217;s first acquisition. The application was built on top of &lt;a href=&quot;http://electron.atom.io/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Electron&lt;/a&gt;, an app framework that enables developers to build cross-platform desktop apps with JavaScript, HTML, and CSS. It allows users to run apache or nginx, switch between PHP versions for any site, create multisite installations (including subdomain setups), and create remote tunnels to share local development. Mac users can download the new Local by Flywheel application at &lt;a href=&quot;http://local.getflywheel.com&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;local.getflywheel.com&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;epoch-width-sniffer&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 01 Dec 2016 15:03:52 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:8;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:46:&quot;HeroPress: WordPressing The Hard Way In Malawi&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:56:&quot;https://heropress.com/?post_type=heropress-essays&amp;p=1502&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:58:&quot;https://heropress.com/essays/wordpressing-hard-way-malawi/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12291:&quot;&lt;img width=&quot;960&quot; height=&quot;480&quot; src=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/113016-1024x512.jpg&quot; class=&quot;attachment-large size-large wp-post-image&quot; alt=&quot;Pull Quote: WordPress has allowed me to find income I otherwise would not have any way in hopes of earning.&quot; /&gt;&lt;p&gt;I am a self-taught graphic designer/ motion designer turned web designer and aspiring web developer from Malawi, Africa. I am a digital tinkerer who has fallen in love with and currently gone steady with WordPress. Still, the journey is rough.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;A little about my home country before you hear my story…&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Malawi&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://www.google.com/search?q=malawi&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;alignright wp-image-1507&quot; src=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/googleit.gif&quot; alt=&quot;Gif of guy reading book, another guy slapping it away, saying Google It&quot; width=&quot;295&quot; height=&quot;166&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Malawi, is at the time of my writing, the poorest country in the world. A tiny land locked country with a population of 17 million, AND still largely rural (about 75%) and struggling to develop.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;The average entry level monthly pay for skilled jobs is about $110.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;You are really fortunate if you are employed, young, working in the creative industry and earning somewhere near $300 a month. I doubt if anybody &lt;em&gt;actually&lt;/em&gt; &lt;strong&gt;employed&lt;/strong&gt; by someone in the design, creative and web services industry earns this much.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;That being said, I have been a freelance graphic designer since about 2011, doing gigs from my dorm room in college and my bedroom at home. Earnings from my freelance gigs increased my interest in entrepreneurship and I soon started entertaining the thought of starting my own creative agency or media powerhouse.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;HOW I FIRST CAME INTO CONTACT WITH WORDPRESS&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I first came into contact with WordPress in 2014 when a friend of mine from University were planning to start a local tech blog. Before WordPress, all I had was basic and outdated HTML knowledge I learned from high school and some knowledge in Adobe Dreamweaver.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In 2014 very few websites in Malawi actually ran on WordPress as far as I remember. Most of the websites made in Malawi looked pretty archaic. With what to me was my partners expertise with WordPress Our blog looked like it came from the future. My partner knew where to get the themes (I did not know how he did it then, and still understood very little about WordPress).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In a little while, ecstatic from the praise and positive feedback from the blog we decided to pursue the idea of opening our own content and media publishing outfit.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Because our blog looked spectacular we got a few web redesign jobs thanks to the exposure the blog brought. We were ecstatic.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Unfortunately, we both had very little administrative and business skills we could not maintain the business and we ended up going our separate ways.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Fast forward post college, out of my first real job that I got in the TV industry ( terrible pay, overworked, and not being paid for about 5 months!) and failing to get more rewarding gigs as my creative agency start up side was cash strapped.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;alignright wp-image-1509&quot; src=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/rowan.gif&quot; alt=&quot;Rowan Atkinson looking shocked&quot; width=&quot;355&quot; height=&quot;200&quot; /&gt;I finally took it upon myself to learn the ins and outs of WordPress. I learned how to install WordPress on a server and did some research on customising Themes. That knowledge alone and presto: I got my first web design clients and started making earning nearly as much as I did at my first job, sometimes a little more, when I get fortunate  some times I even earn three times as much as I used to in a month.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;It only took a very short while for me to realise that free WordPress themes can only go so far, especially with my limited code skills.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;For most WordPress designers in Malawi, all we did was get nulled themes and customise them. This is the way most WordPress designers in developing countries survive. This is also why I would like to build my own themes from scratch, to avoid the situation where I have to use pirated themes that are not only unsafe for clients but unethical. In addition, I know learning to code will also set me apart from my competition.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Which leads me to the next bit….&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;HOW THE LACK OF AN ONLINE PAYMENT SOLUTIONS AFFECTS DESIGNERS/DEVELOPERS IN COUNTRIES LIKE MINE&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;My country apparently has PayPal “available”, but the truth is you cannot get yourself a credit card to be able to join creative markets, and do online courses in order to improve your WP skills. The banks here only issue out credit cards to people who travel overseas or apparently have millions in their bank account.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/city.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;aligncenter wp-image-1510 size-large&quot; src=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/city-1024x576.png&quot; alt=&quot;City Street in Malawi&quot; width=&quot;960&quot; height=&quot;540&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Even so, most of the bank personnel themselves know very little about credit cards and let alone online payment solutions. It is often very frustrating to talk to bank personnel concerning this. Wire transfer and Western Union is still the most popular way to make transactions for goods and services. So many services that we would like to access: plugins, features, etc related to the WP community are far from our reach. The learning and growth often stops the moment you see the “$” sign on websites offering WP solutions and themes.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;THE CHALLENGES OF BEING SELF TAUGHT IN THE DEVELOPING WORLD&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;As I mentioned earlier, I do not have any programming background, I have always been more of a creative and artsy kind of person. Sure I have an eye for design but in order to grow, I need to learn to code PHP, and PHP hard and it is not easy to do so as premium online courses are inaccessible.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;When you are in a position like mine, you are already deep in freelancing and getting a job is currently not the best option because the pay is terrible for people in your industry, and you have to keep on earning, plus make time to learn code. Getting to actually code well is a chore as you have to mind all the other obligations.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Between the time to make pitches to clients, finish up graphic design projects, deal with our current load shedding program (we only have about 5 hours of power a day on average now! ) is something I am barely managing.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Teaching myself code, HTML, CSS,  JavaScript, and PHP for WordPress is something I am determined to do and always in the process of. I try my best to make time to learn. I reckon this would have been easier if I studied a programming course in college but well, here I am.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;WHAT THE WORDPRESS COMMUNITY LOOKS LIKE TO ME&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I will be honest, I have only gotten in touch with the actual WordPress community only very recently. Of course I search for solutions from blogs about WordPress but never actually talked to or asked anyone from the community for a solution. The most personal interaction I have ever had with anyone from the WordPress community is when I talked to &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/topher1kenobe&quot;&gt;Topher&lt;/a&gt; when I applied to write a post for HeroPress.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I often just isolated myself from any attempt to interact at all because of the glass ceiling. There are these feelings you get; these things you tell yourself when you know you can never truly harness the power of WordPress because of your lack of a way to pay for stuff online: You could never be half as good as anyone in developed countries, you will never ever get premium support, you can never be eligible for premium support. I reckon these feelings are worse for people teaching them self how to code like me.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;So when I came across a tweet from &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/heropress&quot;&gt;@HeroPress&lt;/a&gt; about a post that talked about how WordPress marginalises some, it piqued my interest. It was a post from a WordPress developer in India, and it detailed how people from developing countries could never paid the same way someone from the developed countries would for the same skills or services. I totally relate and knew right away I need to sign up to tell my story.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;WordPress designers and wanna-be developers like me (who cannot access online pay systems) often feel side lined.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;When it comes to classes, we stop at the freebies portion, often than not our Google Searches look like this&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;“Free image slider plugins for WordPress” “Free WordPress tutorials”&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I wish more developers, or people with more global privilege would consider alternate ways for users who cannot pay for courses, themes, or plugins would make. We may not seem to be present, but we are there. I would love to see more WordPress tutors and developers open up ways to accommodate aspiring learners like me who cannot access plugins, courses and themes, to be able to give back and to participate at another level.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Many wannabe developers who come from situations similar to mine often shy away from participating with the WordPress community or getting deeper with WordPress because in the ways I have mentioned above, the WordPress community feels like it belongs to those only privileged enough on the internet.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress has allowed me to find income I otherwise would not have any way in hopes of earning. Sure it is lower by global standards, but it makes a huge difference where I live. This is about to be my second year with WordPress, and coming across members of the community with varying backgrounds through HeroPress’ stories tells me there is hope for WordPress users like me.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;I believe through sharing stories like these not only will WordPress products/services be more accessible but aspiring self-taught developers like me will also find more courage in reaching out to connect with others out there.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;

&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:73:&quot;WPTavern: Elizabeth Shilling Awarded the Kim Parsell Memorial Scholarship&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:29:&quot;https://wptavern.com/?p=64044&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:84:&quot;https://wptavern.com/elizabeth-shilling-awarded-the-kim-parsell-memorial-scholarship&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1621:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The WordPress Foundation &lt;a href=&quot;https://2016.us.wordcamp.org/2016/11/24/announcing-the-kim-parsell-memorial-scholarship-winner-elizabeth-shilling/&quot;&gt;has announced&lt;/a&gt; that &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.orcawebperformance.com/&quot;&gt;Elizabeth Shilling&lt;/a&gt;, one of three co-founders of the &lt;a href=&quot;https://womenwhowp.org/&quot;&gt;Women Who WP &lt;/a&gt;meetup group, is the second recipient of the &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/community/2015/01/15/remembering-kim-parsell/&quot;&gt;Kim Parsell Memorial Scholarship&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The scholarship was created in 2015 to remember Kim Parsell and provide an opportunity for a woman who may not have the financial means to attend the largest WordCamp in the US.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;https://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/bridget-elizabeth.jpeg?ssl=1&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-64047&quot; src=&quot;https://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/bridget-elizabeth.jpeg?resize=1025%2C769&amp;ssl=1&quot; alt=&quot;Bridget Willard on the left with Elizabeth Shilling on the right&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Bridget Willard on the left with Elizabeth Shilling on the right
&lt;p&gt;Shilling is a former biology teacher, business owner, plugin developer, and feminist leader. According to the &lt;a href=&quot;https://2016.us.wordcamp.org/2016/11/24/announcing-the-kim-parsell-memorial-scholarship-winner-elizabeth-shilling/&quot;&gt;announcement&lt;/a&gt;, Shilling was chosen for her dedication to open source and being a champion for women in leadership. The scholarship covers the cost of a WordCamp ticket, flight, and lodging. If you see Shilling at WordCamp US this weekend, be sure to congratulate her.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;epoch-width-sniffer&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 29 Nov 2016 22:48:47 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:10;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:77:&quot;WPTavern: PDF Image Previews Among the Improvements to Media in WordPress 4.7&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:29:&quot;https://wptavern.com/?p=64026&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:88:&quot;https://wptavern.com/pdf-image-previews-among-the-improvements-to-media-in-wordpress-4-7&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1840:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Among the many enhancements in WordPress 4.7 are improvements to the media component. Previous to 4.7, users who uploaded files to the media library and changed the title could not search for them by file name. Four years since the &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/22744&quot;&gt;ticket was created&lt;/a&gt;, users will be able to search for media by filename.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;PDFs are &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/11/15/enhanced-pdf-support-4-7/&quot;&gt;easier to preview&lt;/a&gt; as the media library will create an image preview of the first page. This image is used throughout the library and media attachment screens.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;https://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/PDFpreviews.png?ssl=1&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-64027&quot; src=&quot;https://i1.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/PDFpreviews.png?resize=864%2C317&amp;ssl=1&quot; alt=&quot;PDF Preview Images in the WordPress Media Library&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;PDF Preview Images in the WordPress Media Library
&lt;p&gt;In order to generate the previews, the webhosting server needs to support Imagick, ImageMagick, and Ghostscript. If support is not detected, WordPress will fall back and save the attachment without adding a preview image.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.7 also removes the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wptavern.com/wordpress-4-7-improves-accessibility-by-removing-alternative-text-fallbacks&quot;&gt;caption text and the image title fallbacks&lt;/a&gt; to generate alternative text. Developers are encouraged to read the &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/11/15/enhanced-pdf-support-4-7/&quot;&gt;detailed notes&lt;/a&gt; surrounding PDF previews to ensure compatibility with WordPress 4.7. There&amp;#8217;s also a handful of other changes to media that users and developers can &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/11/22/media-changes-in-4-7/&quot;&gt;read here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;epoch-width-sniffer&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 29 Nov 2016 01:41:53 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:11;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:41:&quot;Dev Blog: WordPress 4.7 Release Candidate&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:34:&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/?p=4579&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:67:&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/11/wordpress-4-7-release-candidate/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4302:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The release candidate for WordPress 4.7 is now available.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;RC means we think we’re done, but with millions of users and thousands of plugins and themes, it’s possible we’ve missed something. We hope to ship WordPress 4.7 on &lt;strong&gt;Tuesday, December 6&lt;/strong&gt;, but we need &lt;em&gt;your&lt;/em&gt; help to get there. If you haven’t tested 4.7 yet, now is the time! To test WordPress 4.7, you can use the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/plugins/wordpress-beta-tester/&quot;&gt;WordPress Beta Tester&lt;/a&gt; plugin or you can &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/wordpress-4.7-RC1.zip&quot;&gt;download the release candidate here&lt;/a&gt; (zip).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 4.7 is a jam-packed release, with a number of features focused on getting a theme set up for the first time. Highlights include a &lt;a href=&quot;http://2017.wordpress.net/&quot;&gt;new default theme&lt;/a&gt;, video headers, custom CSS, customizer edit shortcuts, PDF thumbnail previews, user admin languages, REST API content endpoints, post type templates, and more.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We’ve made &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/log/trunk/src?action=stop_on_copy&amp;mode=stop_on_copy&amp;rev=39353&amp;stop_rev=39263&amp;limit=200&amp;verbose=on&amp;sfp_email=&amp;sfph_mail=&quot;&gt;quite a few refinements&lt;/a&gt; since releasing Beta 4 a week ago, including usability and accessibility enhancements for video headers, media and page template support in starter content, and polishing of how custom CSS can be migrated to and extended by plugins and themes. The REST API endpoints saw a number of bugfixes and notably now have anonymous comment off by default.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Not sure where to start with testing? Try setting up a fresh site on a new installation with Twenty Seventeen (hint: head into customizing your site before touching any pages or widgets) and taking notes on what you enjoyed and what got you stuck. For more details about what&amp;#8217;s new in version 4.7, check out the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/10/wordpress-4-7-beta-1/&quot;&gt;Beta 1&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/11/wordpress-4-7-beta-2/&quot;&gt;Beta 2&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/11/wordpress-4-7-beta-3/&quot;&gt;Beta 3&lt;/a&gt;, and &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/news/2016/11/wordpress-4-7-beta-4/&quot;&gt;Beta 4&lt;/a&gt; blog posts.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Think you’ve found a bug?&lt;/strong&gt; Please post to the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpress.org/support/forum/alphabeta/&quot;&gt;Alpha/Beta support forum&lt;/a&gt;. If any known issues come up, you’ll be able to &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/report/5&quot;&gt;find them here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Developers&lt;/strong&gt;, please test your plugins and themes against WordPress 4.7 and update your plugin’s &lt;em&gt;Tested up to&lt;/em&gt; version in the readme to 4.7. If you find compatibility problems please be sure to post to the support forums so we can figure those out before the final release – we work hard to avoid breaking things. An in-depth field guide to developer-focused changes is coming soon on the &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/&quot;&gt;core development blog&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Do you speak a language other than English? &lt;a href=&quot;https://translate.wordpress.org/projects/wp/dev&quot;&gt;Help us translate WordPress into more than 100 languages!&lt;/a&gt; And if you haven&amp;#8217;t yet done so, now is a great time to &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpressdotorg.polldaddy.com/s/wordpress-2016-survey&quot;&gt;take the Annual WordPress Survey&lt;/a&gt; and send it on to your friends.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Happy testing! And now for another &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/ramiabraham&quot;&gt;Rami Abraham&lt;/a&gt; haiku break.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;em&gt;Then let your users choose theirs&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;

&lt;em&gt;Less laconic lists&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 24 Nov 2016 04:26:23 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:15:&quot;Helen Hou-Sandi&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:12;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:45:&quot;WPTavern: Why Are You Thankful for WordPress?&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:29:&quot;https://wptavern.com/?p=64012&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:55:&quot;https://wptavern.com/why-are-you-thankful-for-wordpress&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3836:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Tomorrow is Thanksgiving in the US. It&amp;#8217;s a time of reflection and an opportunity to express gratitude for the good things in life. In &lt;a href=&quot;http://kitchensinkwp.com/podcast-e143-thankgiving-wordpress-2016/&quot;&gt;episode 143&lt;/a&gt; of the KitchensinkWP podcast, host Adam Silver asked his two sons why they&amp;#8217;re grateful for WordPress.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;I am thankful for WordPress because it gives you a job for the household that we live in and it makes you happy which also makes me happy and smile,&amp;#8221; Parker said. &amp;#8220;I am thankful for WordPress because it makes you happy and it makes me happy and it provides a roof over our heads,&amp;#8221; Carson said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Inspired by the episode, &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/josheby&quot;&gt;Josh Eby&lt;/a&gt; created the &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/hashtag/Thankful4WP?src=hash&quot;&gt;#Thankful4WP&lt;/a&gt; hashtag on Twitter. Here are a few reasons why people are thankful for WordPress.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot;&gt;&lt;p lang=&quot;en&quot; dir=&quot;ltr&quot;&gt;My &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/hashtag/Thankful4WP?src=hash&quot;&gt;#Thankful4WP&lt;/a&gt; List:&lt;br /&gt;* Life I enjoy because of WP&lt;br /&gt;* Lifelong, &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/hashtag/Iceberg?src=hash&quot;&gt;#Iceberg&lt;/a&gt; friendships&lt;br /&gt;* Passionate &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/ithemes&quot;&gt;@ithemes&lt;/a&gt; team&lt;br /&gt;* Customers who support us&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;mdash; Cory Miller (@corymiller303) &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/corymiller303/status/801458665790304256&quot;&gt;November 23, 2016&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot;&gt;&lt;p lang=&quot;en&quot; dir=&quot;ltr&quot;&gt;My &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/hashtag/Thankful4WP?src=hash&quot;&gt;#Thankful4WP&lt;/a&gt; list: the awesome community, resources, WordCamps, building websites w/ WP, the people, oh and did I mention the people? ❤️&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;mdash; Justine Pretorious (@jpretorious) &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/jpretorious/status/801334701306875905&quot;&gt;November 23, 2016&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;

&lt;p&gt;&amp;mdash; Susan Ramsey (@onehappystudio) &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/onehappystudio/status/801226653435396096&quot;&gt;November 23, 2016&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
