&lt;div id=&quot;epoch-width-sniffer&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 10 Nov 2016 20:53:21 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:35;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:91:&quot;WPTavern: WordPress Community Team Proposes New Selection Process for 2017 Summit Attendees&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:29:&quot;https://wptavern.com/?p=63604&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:102:&quot;https://wptavern.com/wordpress-community-team-proposes-new-selection-process-for-2017-summit-attendees&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4890:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/testing.jpg?ssl=1&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;https://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/07/testing.jpg?resize=960%2C474&amp;ssl=1&quot; alt=&quot;testing&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-46092&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordCamp Europe 2017 is set to &lt;a href=&quot;https://wptavern.com/wordcamp-europe-2017-will-host-the-next-wordpress-community-summit&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;host the next community summit&lt;/a&gt; in Paris. This will be the first time the event has been held outside of the United States, a change that makes it more accessible for contributors who are unable to obtain a visa to enter the U.S.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Attaching the summit to WordCamp Europe was the next logical step, as the event brings together project contributors from around the world. Europe is one of the fastest growing regions for the WordPress community in terms of events, with a &lt;a href=&quot;https://wptavern.com/europe-tops-wordcamp-growth-in-2015-with-70-increase-in-events&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;70% increase in WordCamps in 2015&lt;/a&gt;. There were 20 WordCamps held in October and 50% of those were hosted in European cities.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The past three community summits have been invitation-only in order to ensure those present were active contributors to WordPress and to enable a format that facilitates face-to-face discussions on key issues facing the project and the community. This inevitably leaves many valuable contributors on the outside. In an effort to mitigate the sense of exclusivity around the event, the WordPress Community Team is &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/community/2016/11/03/wordpress-community-summit-2017/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;proposing a new selection process for 2017&lt;/a&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;If we have to limit our attendance to have productive, collaborative discussions at the Summit, then choosing the participants becomes a challenge if we don’t know what the teams are going to discuss ahead of time. Therefore, this year I suggest we try something new:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Let’s ask teams to decide on the challenging, controversial, or sensitive issues they want to discuss at the summit before the summit is held. Then, once the teams know what they want to talk over in person, they can nominate and select the people needed to represent all points of view in each of those discussions. This way, the event stays small, hard topics get discussed, but the selection process is more transparent and functional.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Rocio Valdivia, who posted the proposal on behalf of the team, roughly outlined how the selection process would work. She suggested each make.wordpress.org project team would create and publish a list of topics/issues for discussion at the summit and submit them by December 20th. Teams would then select representatives to attend the summit. Two members of those selected would be assigned to help with the organization and logistics of the summit, including tasks such as finding sponsors, travel assistance, and communication.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;The intention of this approach is to propose a more open and team-focus Community Summit with transparent participation from all active contributors and reps of each team,&amp;#8221; Valdivia said. &amp;#8220;This way we can hopefully anticipate barriers and cross-team difficulties that might come up, and avoid them.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This approach is different from past events where attendees were not part of the organizational aspects but it gives contributors more ownership of the event and their teams&amp;#8217; specific goals. Details and logistics would be worked out later in the year with the help of the WCEU organizers.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The Community Team is asking for feedback on the &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/community/2016/11/03/wordpress-community-summit-2017/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;proposal&lt;/a&gt; before implementing a plan of action for the new selection process. As the open source project has grown, WordPress has hundreds of contributors spread across its three dozen core &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/components/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;components&lt;/a&gt;. So far contributors have weighed in on the initial proposed number of team representatives and the deadline for preparing topics.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;There was also some concern in the Community Team&amp;#8217;s meeting on Slack as to whether the new selection process will perpetuate the pattern of the same people being invited to the summit every time simply because they are most active in the project. Allowing teams to nominate their representatives based on the anticipated topics will make the selection process more focused on which contributors are best suited to work on pressing issues. Moving the location to Europe will also give regional contributors the opportunity to bring fresh ideas and perspectives, especially regarding the challenges of multilingual publishing with WordPress.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;epoch-width-sniffer&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 10 Nov 2016 06:48:23 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:36;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:47:&quot;bbPress: bbPress 2.5.11 – Maintenance Release&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:29:&quot;https://bbpress.org/?p=178971&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:68:&quot;https://bbpress.org/blog/2016/11/bbpress-2-5-11-maintenance-release/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1075:&quot;&lt;p&gt;bbPress 2.5.11 is out, and is a maintenance release for all previous 2.x versions. 2.5.11 includes support for the soon to be released WordPress 4.7. If you&amp;#8217;re planning on updating to WordPress 4.7 right away, you&amp;#8217;ll want to update to bbPress 2.5.11 immediately.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you&amp;#8217;re using any version of bbPress 2.x and have not yet updated, please take a moment to update your bbPress installations to 2.5.11. If you&amp;#8217;re using WordPress&amp;#8217;s built-in updater, it should only take a click or two. If you need help, please reach out in our &lt;a href=&quot;https://bbpress.org/forums/&quot;&gt;support forums&lt;/a&gt; and someone will be happy to assist you.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;These fixes have also been ported over to 2.6, which we continue to run here at bbPress.org and BuddyPress.org.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;hr /&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Speaking of bbPress 2.6, per-forum moderators, favorites, and subscriptions are fully refactored and working pretty great. Our findings have also helped push performance improvements upstream to WordPress core, and are already employed across the forums on WordPress.org.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 10 Nov 2016 00:27:22 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:17:&quot;John James Jacoby&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:37;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:103:&quot;WPTavern: A New Way to Search, Preview, and Install Themes in the Customizer Removed From WordPress 4.7&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:29:&quot;https://wptavern.com/?p=63634&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:112:&quot;https://wptavern.com/a-new-way-to-search-preview-and-install-themes-in-the-customizer-removed-from-wordpress-4-7&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4376:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Astute testers may have noticed a new feature in WordPress 4.7 beta 1 that enabled users to search, preview, and install themes from within the customizer. This feature was part of &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/10/24/customize-update-2016-10-23/&quot;&gt;five feature projects&lt;/a&gt; related to the customizer that were approved for merge last month. Its goal is to &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/core/2016/10/03/feature-proposal-a-new-experience-for-discovering-installing-and-previewing-themes-in-the-customizer/&quot;&gt;unify the theme browsing and customizing experience&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;https://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/CustomizerThemeBrowserFlow.png?ssl=1&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-63638&quot; src=&quot;https://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/CustomizerThemeBrowserFlow.png?resize=1025%2C793&amp;ssl=1&quot; alt=&quot;Customizer Theme Browser Flow&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Customizer Theme Browser Flow
&lt;p&gt;It was removed in WordPress 4.7 beta 2. Helen Hou-Sandí, WordPress 4.7 release lead, &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/37661#comment:121&quot;&gt;reverted the change&lt;/a&gt; after &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/37661#comment:113&quot;&gt;collecting feedback. &lt;/a&gt;Some of the reasons for reverting the feature include:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Displaying on mobile devices is broken.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Inability to close the feature/filter accordion.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Checkmarks are overlayed on top of the search form.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;The full-screen plus reload experience isn&amp;#8217;t polished.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/37661#comment:121&quot;&gt;According to Hou-Sandí&lt;/a&gt;, there is not enough time left in the development cycle to polish the design and make it sufficient for WordPress 4.7. Nick Halsey, who helps maintain the Customizer component, &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/37661#comment:127&quot;&gt;expressed displeasure&lt;/a&gt; with the decision.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Abruptly deciding to pull something without allowing any opportunity to improve things or even bring it up in a weekly dev chat is ridiculous,&amp;#8221; Halsey said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Had I been asked to provide patches for outstanding bugs (one of which never even received a ticket), I would have gladly done so sooner &amp;#8211; this was my highest priority for core for the past 4 months.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Halsey goes on to say that the revert is disrespectful and insulting to him and that he is unlikely to further contribute to the project until it is back in trunk. Samuel Sidler, &lt;span class=&quot;st&quot;&gt;Apollo Team Lead at Automattic&lt;/span&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/37661#comment:124&quot;&gt;responded to Halsey &lt;/a&gt;supporting Hou-Sandí&amp;#8217;s decision.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Making a decision to pull a highly visible feature is hard, but, as you know, it&amp;#8217;s ultimately one that the release lead should make as it&amp;#8217;s &lt;em&gt;their release&lt;/em&gt; and they have the best overall view,&amp;#8221; Sidler said.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Weston Ruter, who also helps maintain the Customizer component, asked if the revert could be reversed if patches to outstanding issues were created.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;No &amp;#8211; if this were a matter of problems that have defined solutions already then the course of action would not have been a revert,&amp;#8221; Hou-Sandí &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/37661#comment:130&quot;&gt;responded&lt;/a&gt;. &amp;#8220;I know that it would feel better to have something more than &amp;#8216;my gut and the guts of others say no&amp;#8217;, but if there was more definition to the problems then we may not have been in a position where reverting from this release was the only sane thing to do.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/37661&quot;&gt;feature has been punted&lt;/a&gt; and the milestone was changed from WordPress 4.7 to a Future Release.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;A Window Into How WordPress Development Works&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The quotes I published above are only part of the story. I highly encourage you to start with &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/37661#comment:113&quot;&gt;this post&lt;/a&gt; and read every response in full. It&amp;#8217;s a great opportunity to see a WordPress release lead in action and how and why certain decisions in WordPress development are made. Those interested in the feature&amp;#8217;s progress can follow along by &lt;a href=&quot;https://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/37661&quot;&gt;monitoring this ticket&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;epoch-width-sniffer&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Wed, 09 Nov 2016 23:41:48 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:38;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:49:&quot;HeroPress: Uncomfortable doesn’t mean walk away&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:56:&quot;https://heropress.com/?post_type=heropress-essays&amp;p=1466&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:65:&quot;https://heropress.com/essays/uncomfortable-doesnt-mean-walk-away/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:23144:&quot;&lt;img width=&quot;960&quot; height=&quot;480&quot; src=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/110916-1024x512.jpg&quot; class=&quot;attachment-large size-large wp-post-image&quot; alt=&quot;Pull Quote: Uncomfortable often means there is something amazing to be learnt.&quot; /&gt;&lt;p&gt;I am not a developer. Confession? It feels like it sometimes. In my mind’s eye I see a roomful of skittish WordPress marketers with dark-ringed eyes, disclosing the number of times they pretended to understand something technical when it made about as much sense to them as the moon landing. Frustrated they can’t code it themselves. Maybe it’s just me in that room.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I am a words person – a creative, a copywriter, and a marketer. My heart beats faster over ancient English literature, clever mailers, alliteration, storytelling and subject lines, and the shapeshifting challenge of building an authentic brand in a world of smoke, mirrors, and shmoozing.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Topher asked me to write my WordPress story and when I thought about what I’ve learnt over the past two years what came to mind was: &lt;strong&gt;uncomfortable doesn’t mean walk away&lt;/strong&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Far from being something to categorically flee or avoid, discomfort is a signpost to watch out for – something to embrace and step bravely towards. Obviously there are exceptions – but in my experience discomfort often means lean in, listen closely, change something.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I’ve chosen to share a few of the ways I’ve encountered uncomfortable in my WordPress journey so far, and why I’m grateful.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;A bit of background&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Perhaps we are all creatures of habit on some level, but I really am. For example, when backpacking with my best friend in 2008 from Istanbul down to Cairo – through Syria and Jordan, including places that are now literally non-existent – she and I noticed that if we found a good restaurant I’d suggest returning the following night while she always wanted to try new spots.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;When I find something I like, it makes perfect sense to me to stick with it, sometimes to a fault. Until fairly recently I would have described myself as someone who didn’t thrive on change. This partly explains why by the age of twenty nine my entire life had played out in one city.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/IMG_5951-min.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-large wp-image-1470&quot; src=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/IMG_5951-min-1024x768.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;Marina as a child with mother&quot; width=&quot;960&quot; height=&quot;720&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;My beautiful mum, brother and I. My mum is a superhuman and I miss her daily.
&lt;p&gt;Birth, preschool to postgraduate studies, the first nine years of my career, family, friends, life – all in one patch.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I have been privileged to do some excellent travelling to amazing places – European beach holidays and ski trips (obviously I broke my arm), teaching English for four weeks in South Korea, a cruise in Alaska, a church trip to Singapore and Malaysia, Vancouver to visit family – but my sense of home and place was unwaveringly Cape Town.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;At the beginning of 2014 I decided to emigrate. The delay between the idea occurring to me and resigning was less than two weeks. With a British passport through my English mum and a mild obsession with all things British, London was it. It seemed wise to secure a job first but my gut said I should have faith and move regardless so I resigned from Yuppiechef.com &lt;a href=&quot;https://www.yuppiechef.com/spatula/10-thoughts-about-community-management-and-social-media/&quot;&gt;where I’d been for nearly five years&lt;/a&gt;, sold my car, and booked a one way ticket.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;At this point, it would be fair to say WordPress was not even really on my radar. It powered Yuppiechef’s blog so I’d used it in that capacity and &lt;a href=&quot;https://marinapape.com/&quot;&gt;my own blog&lt;/a&gt; was on WordPress.com – but it was pretty much just a thing to do with the internet that helped people publish stuff.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;A week before I set off I was having sushi with friends and got chatting to a mouthy American who worked for WooThemes. Hearing of my pending departure and getting a sense of my strengths and what I loved to do, he suggested I consider applying. Less than a week later I accepted an offer to join Woo’s then-tiny marketing team. I’m still amazed at the speed with which it all happened – and will be forever amused by Mark and Warren’s confidence in me as a total WordPress n0ob (maybe they didn’t realise!).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/IMG_8001-min.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-large wp-image-1471&quot; src=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/IMG_8001-min-1024x768.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;I love MailChimp. Freddy lives on my desk beside some Woo stickers&quot; width=&quot;960&quot; height=&quot;720&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;I love MailChimp. Freddy lives on my desk beside some Woo stickers
&lt;p&gt;And so my WordPress journey began in London on 1 July 2014, fresh off the boat and working remotely for the first time. I logged online from a coffee shop – specifically Timberyard, which has become a familiar friend – and dived headfirst into a world I hadn’t realised would be so technical. And digital. Marketing a digital product is a very different kettle of fish to kitchen products. And working remotely as an extrovert?&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In my first week I was sent to WordCamp Brighton where I innocently asked someone the difference between .org and WordPress.com. This was the first prickle of my first uncomfortable hurdle: being okay with not knowing everything.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;It really is okay not to know everything.&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;It sounds stupid to even write that one needs to be okay with not knowing everything – of course one can’t, but at Yuppiechef.com I sure knew a lot more about a lot more. There, my lack of technical understanding wasn’t a thing, marketing was lauded, and our brand was at the forefront of what set us apart. &lt;a href=&quot;http://ventureburn.com/2013/03/the-yuppiechef-cult-how-a-startup-sparked-a-religion/&quot;&gt;People wrote about how the following for Yuppiechef was cult-like&lt;/a&gt;, and I’d helped create that.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Joining Woo I was a tiny fish all over again, and I was swimming in a world with languages I didn’t understand.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Everyone is a genius. But if you judge a fish by its ability to climb a tree, it will live its whole life believing that it is stupid. – unknown (but attributed to Einstein)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;It was a little bit terrifying to be a marketer in this tech-celebratory world. And it took me a long time to accept I have something significant to offer at WooCommerce (and now Automattic) and feel confident enough to add my voice to conversations. Why? I guess I am proud. In the early days I was constantly tempted to pretend to know more than I do (for the record this is a bad idea) and developed a hefty dose of imposter syndrome, which worsened when Automattic acquired WooCommerce. I found myself wondering if they would have hired me.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;For a few months, the fear I felt kept me from bringing to the table the valuable things I did know.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/IMG_7373-min.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-large wp-image-1472&quot; src=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/IMG_7373-min-1024x768.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;Standing by a concrete wall with a vast ocean scene behind.&quot; width=&quot;960&quot; height=&quot;720&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;With my team in Cape Town earlier this year. Nicole, Aviva, me, Gareth and Kevin &amp;lt;3.
&lt;p&gt;It’s scary admitting a lack of understanding, it takes strong relationships with colleagues (which take time to build, especially remotely) to raise your hand and be vulnerable. But the problem is that not doing so ends up blocking and robbing the contribution you could make. It silences your voice. It is not possible to be a master of all trades: yes I need a working understanding of our products, but I don’t need to become a Javascript developer. One body, many parts, all valuable.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This learning curve was uncomfortable for me. At various points I have wanted to bail, or take a year to learn how to code fulltime. But I am really glad I haven’t because marketing is vital and that is what I can do. And do very well (when I’m not looking over my shoulder).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;It’s okay to be an expert in what you love, not what other people love. It’s why we have teams. It’s what makes the world interesting.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/IMG_3576-min.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-large wp-image-1473&quot; src=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/IMG_3576-min-1024x768.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;Classroom filled with people&quot; width=&quot;960&quot; height=&quot;720&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;The first WordPress London meetup I attended. It was pretty awesome.
&lt;h3&gt;Remote relationships take longer to build but they sure run deep.&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;My degree was in Psychology and it remains an active interest. ENFJ is proudly in my Twitter bio, I love taking personality tests and calling out and connecting with the underbellies and depths of fellow human beings.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;&lt;strong&gt;My friends are my estate&lt;/strong&gt;. Forgive me then the avarice to hoard them.&amp;#8221; – Emily Dickinson&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you’re familiar with Gallups Strengthfinder, I’m a Relator to the bone. People often ask how I have the discipline to work from home but that’s pocket change compared to the relational challenge. Showing up to work and being productive hasn’t been the thing I’ve found difficult – it’s trying to build relationship digitally with people far away and in different timezones.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Plus I find there is a certain type of rapport, creativity, and energy that is really hard to create remotely when it comes to brainstorming and collaborating. The buzz of having an idea and someone else adding to it IRL, growing it into something greater. This was not a comfortable thing, but again choosing to stay has proven invaluable.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Remote relationships take longer to build, but they sure run deep&lt;/strong&gt;. The bonding that happens when you come together for meetups and WordCamps is extraordinary. I have grown to properly know and love my colleagues (not all 500+ Automatticians yet but certainly my immediate team) and a bunch of awesome WordPress people I’ve met.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/IMG_8319-min.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-large wp-image-1474&quot; src=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/IMG_8319-min-1024x768.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;On-screen grid of faces in a google hangout&quot; width=&quot;960&quot; height=&quot;720&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Well hello Woo people. Here’s us hanging out on Air.
&lt;p&gt;It’s tiring flying to meetups, and you miss home, but it’s now becoming hard to leave them. My heart sometimes feels like it is scattered in little bits: a fragment with Scotty and the Dekode crew in Norway, another few with Louise in Kwazulu Natal, Cobus and Dom in Cape Town and chunks with Nicole and Aviva stateside. It’s fragmenting, but what a privilege.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;To keep me grounded day to day, I’ve helped start and now am involved in running a non-profit coworking space, which has opened up a whole new web of relationships in London. If you’re ever in town, pop into &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.arkcoworking.com/&quot;&gt;ARK Coworking&lt;/a&gt; for a pour over coffee.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Working remotely is different. But it’s a pretty niche kind of special to have a web of people around the world that you would otherwise be totally unconnected to.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/IMG_4183-min.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-1475&quot; src=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/IMG_4183-min.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;People standing astride bikes, flashing gang symbols.&quot; width=&quot;749&quot; height=&quot;549&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;The Woo biker gang on a marketing meetup near Lake Michigan, 2015
&lt;p&gt;Which brings me to another uncomfortable hurdle brought squarely to me by WordPress: the challenge of responding well to diversity and difference.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Thinking something for a long time doesn’t mean it’s true.&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Part of &lt;a href=&quot;https://automattic.com/creed/&quot;&gt;Automattic’s creed&lt;/a&gt; is to never stop learning. Being part of WordPress has brought me into close proximity with a more varied, vocal, challenging, and diverse group than I could have made up.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The thing about being a human is you only ever get to be one of them. One in over seven billion. How much about other people and parts of the world you don’t live in do you know, really? How much do I? Being part of WordPress has opened my eyes to diversity in a way that is hard to describe. Emigrating helped too, but it is very possible to live in a bubble wherever you go.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;A long habit of not thinking a thing wrong gives it a superficial appearance of being right. – Thomas Paine&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Just because something has always been a certain way, doesn’t make it right. Being part of WordPress, and Automattic, has helped me greatly in learning how to hold what I believe to be right and true gently, and have equal respect for other people’s right and true.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I ran the WooCommerce London meetup for two years which brought me into contact with a very mixed group; I was part of Automattic’s diversity workshop at the GM which was educational to say the least; when my friend Rosie started a &lt;a href=&quot;http://mouthywomen.work/&quot;&gt;blog&lt;/a&gt; to highlight out how mouthy women get told they’re too masculine, I got behind her heart and soul.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/Screen-Shot-2016-11-03-at-13.21.46-min.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;wp-image-1476 size-full&quot; src=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/Screen-Shot-2016-11-03-at-13.21.46-min.png&quot; alt=&quot;Stewart Ritchie sharing at the WooCommerce London meetup. Photo: Gabor Javorsky.&quot; width=&quot;601&quot; height=&quot;447&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Stewart Ritchie sharing at the WooCommerce London meetup. Photo: Gabor Javorsky.
&lt;p&gt;The most poignant example of this for me was much closer to home. I wrote some copy a while ago as the backstory of Woo’s ninja mascot, Hiro and included in it a bunch of references to Japanese culture that, though well intentioned, turned out to be not okay. It had been up for ages before someone with a different enough perspective flagged it. Ouch.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I went home after a long day of tears and much Slack messaging and confided in my Malaysian flatmate about it, half expecting him to comfort me and say the whole thing really wasn’t such a big deal and that it didn’t bother him. Instead his only comment was: “&lt;em&gt;That’s good. It will make your company better.&lt;/em&gt;”&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We live, we learn. We wound, we grow.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;John Maeda, who recently joined Automattic as Head of Design and Inclusion, calls such oversights in our thinking ‘lacunae’. Being part of the worldwide community of WordPress has brought a number of my own lacunae into sharp focus. It’s also made me more able to exist peacefully alongside people whose views I don’t share. I’m a human, they’re a human. Two in seven billion.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Now, the idea of stepping away and retreating to a more homogenous, same-y group of people who tend to agree with me is not just unattractive, it’s scary.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress helps me be open-minded and it’s vehicle for doing this is individuals who are willing to speak up. Let’s help each other, as kindly and graciously as we can.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Marketing a WordPress product is difficult.&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I’ve found marketing WooCommerce challenging for two reasons.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;First there is the classic digital marketer’s problem of how to build relationship with customers you never get to meet. All we have are words online and if we’re lucky some rituals and routines we can inject life into (I wrote about this strategy &lt;a href=&quot;https://woocommerce.com/2015/11/4-customer-rituals/&quot;&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Over the past two years there have been a number of times I have thrown my hands up in the air and wanted to market something that is just easier to sell (coffee, an awesome gadget, luxury jewelry).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;On top of that eCommerce is a competitive space and selling WordPress can be a little complex messaging-wise, especially for non-coders and those not familiar with WordPress:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Friend: Do I even have WooCommerce yet?&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;em&gt; Me: Yes it’s there in your downloads folder.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;em&gt; Friend: &lt;span&gt;&amp;lt;silence&amp;gt;&lt;/span&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Every time I see another seductive Squarespace ad or the daily Shopify case study lands in my inbox (&lt;em&gt;How person x built y and changed the destiny of the human race&lt;/em&gt;) – part of me can only see how far we have to go.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;But, I am enjoying fighting the good fight to democratise eCommerce with WordPress. I believe in what we’re doing, and in open source, and even though our competitors have bigger marketing teams and 24/7 phone support I feel a fierce loyalty to Woo.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I don’t believe marketing has the emphasis it deserves in the WordPress space, but it’s coming to the fore. Great products don’t market themselves. The weaker thing will win if that is what is in front of people. I’m excited to be in this space.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Saying less is more. Narrow focus is healthy.&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;As someone who loves to joke around, natter, and come up with ideas, something I have learnt the hard way is that volume of words and number of ideas is not no an indicator of the quality of your contribution.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;It feels nice to be busy, but what is the deliverable?&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Having another great idea is not always helpful. Sometimes what I need to do is shut up and work. The manager versus maker ratio tends to leave a lot of cooks in the kitchen. Ideas are a dime a dozen. Pushing a few strategic things over the line, with your eyes on a goal everyone has agreed on, now that’s a better way.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Staying focused working remotely can be hard. Fortunately, we have a great system of setting OKRs that my team is particularly diligent at sticking to. There are so. Many. Conversations. Going on all of the time. Focus is a healthy and freeing thing.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/IMG_4139-min.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-large wp-image-1477&quot; src=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/IMG_4139-min-1024x768.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;Marina and Louise, heads together, grinning&quot; width=&quot;960&quot; height=&quot;720&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;My Woo bestie, Louise. Here we are in San Francisco in 2014. I went back to South Africa for her wedding this year :).
&lt;h3&gt;Inclusion is a very important thing.&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;A final thing I am learning through WordPress, and which has made my uncomfortable for sure, is the importance of inclusion. I touched on this a little already, but it’s something that I have now got my teeth into and am not going to let go of. Inclusion is a thing.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Something that is great about WordPress is that intrinsically inclusive, it’s open to all.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;It isn’t only about big shiny success stories where people are making thousands of dollars. It’s people all over the world, fighting to make WordPress available in all languages; it’s faithful meetup organisers sharing knowledge with those who are just starting out; it’s the GPL; it’s having childcare at WordCamps; it’s using &lt;em&gt;y’all&lt;/em&gt; or &lt;em&gt;folks&lt;/em&gt; not &lt;em&gt;guys&lt;/em&gt; to greet an audience.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress is not slick, sometimes things get a bit messy and there are heated discussions on forums and in backchannels. But WordPress is also a lot like how the world should be – democratic, going out of it’s way to make room and include, and with more than just the bottom line driving decisions.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Conclusion&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;That’s it from me. I hope sharing just a few of the ways WordPress has made me uncomfortable– what I learnt, and why I am glad I didn’t just bail – will be encouraging.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Perhaps you are facing some tough things related to work or beyond. Maybe someone has expressed an opinion or belief that has made you uncomfortable. I’d encourage you to pause and take some time to think over whatever it is before acting.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;Uncomfortable often means there is something amazing to be learnt.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Let’s be brave, open, and keep on learning together through this wonderful thing called WordPress.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/IMG_4832-min.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;alignnone size-large wp-image-1478&quot; src=&quot;http://20094-presscdn.pagely.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/11/IMG_4832-min-1024x768.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;Pin board with hundreds of photos all over it.&quot; width=&quot;960&quot; height=&quot;720&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:83:&quot;WPTavern: BuddyPress 2.8 Development Kicks Off, 2016 Survey Now Open for Developers&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:29:&quot;https://wptavern.com/?p=63402&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:93:&quot;https://wptavern.com/buddypress-2-8-development-kicks-off-2016-survey-now-open-for-developers&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3278:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/buddypress-logo-blue.png?ssl=1&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;https://i0.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/buddypress-logo-blue.png?resize=839%2C398&amp;ssl=1&quot; alt=&quot;buddypress-logo-blue&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-30655&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Development for BuddyPress 2.8 kicked off during &lt;a href=&quot;https://bpdevel.wordpress.com/2016/11/05/dev-chat-summary-for-november-2-2016/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;last week&amp;#8217;s meeting&lt;/a&gt; and the target release date was set for January 25. In line with the project&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;https://wptavern.com/buddypress-2-7-development-kicks-off-project-shifts-focus-to-developers-and-site-builders&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;recent change of course&lt;/a&gt;, the upcoming release will be another one focused on developers and site builders.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Long time contributor &lt;a href=&quot;https://profiles.wordpress.org/slaFFik&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Slava Abakumov&lt;/a&gt; is leading 2.8 with a focus on reducing the 650+ tickets in BuddyPress Trac by 50%. He will coordinate contributors in working on a UI for developer features that were added in the 2.6 and 2.7 releases, which introduced an API for Group Types. Abakumov wants to dive deeper into security and plans to perform a security audit of the plugin.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The BuddyPress core team will shape development for 2017 based on feedback from this year&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;https://buddypress.org/2016/11/2016-buddypress-survey-site-builders-developers/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;survey&lt;/a&gt;, which opened November 1. It includes 36 questions aimed at site builders and developers, as opposed to previous years where the survey was &lt;a href=&quot;https://buddypress.org/2014/01/2014-buddypress-survey/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;open to users and anyone connected with the software&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The project&amp;#8217;s change of direction is evident in the questions this year, which are decidedly developer-focused. According to the BuddyPress core team, these questions were prepared for the project&amp;#8217;s primary audience of site builders and developers, &amp;#8220;an explicit recognition of what BuddyPress has become, and how people use it.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In addition to the usual demographical questions, respondents are asked about their PHP versions, site setups, and local development environments. A new question asks when developers test their sites and extensions against upcoming releases. The survey also asks which template files developers customize when creating themes (with no option to indicate that you&amp;#8217;re not a theme developer). Participants are asked to weigh in on BuddyPress&amp;#8217; problem areas and to give feedback on the most frequent feature requests they receive from community members and clients.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In 2013 the survey received 178 responses, 338 responses in 2014, and 211 in 2015. Given that the target audience is much narrower in 2016, the number of participants may decline again. However, the core team hopes responses will be more concentrated with the kind of information they find useful. The &lt;a href=&quot;https://buddypress.org/2016/11/2016-buddypress-survey-site-builders-developers/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;survey&lt;/a&gt; will be open through November 20, 2016 and results will be posted before the end of the year.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;epoch-width-sniffer&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 08 Nov 2016 18:17:40 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:40;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:55:&quot;WPTavern: WordCamp US Live Stream Tickets Now Available&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:29:&quot;https://wptavern.com/?p=63030&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:66:&quot;https://wptavern.com/wordcamp-us-live-stream-tickets-now-available&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:2838:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/wordcamp-us.png?ssl=1&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;https://i2.wp.com/wptavern.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/wordcamp-us.png?resize=1025%2C490&amp;ssl=1&quot; alt=&quot;wordcamp-us&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-full wp-image-59619&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://2016.us.wordcamp.org&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WordCamp US&lt;/a&gt; is less than a month away and attendees are finalizing their travel plans. In August, organizers were &lt;a href=&quot;https://wptavern.com/wordcamp-us-calls-for-volunteers-organizers-estimate-3000-attendees&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;estimating 3,000 attendees&lt;/a&gt; on the ground but official numbers are not yet available as tickets continue to sell. A maximum capacity has not been published, because organizers have a great deal of flexibility to expand the event to thousands more if necessary.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;The entire side of the PA Convention Center is ours, and we’re not using all of the spaces that they have,&amp;#8221; WordCamp US co-organizer Alx Block said. &amp;#8220;The sky is the limit.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Last week a world-class lineup of &lt;a href=&quot;https://2016.us.wordcamp.org/speakers/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;speakers&lt;/a&gt; was confirmed from a record number of applicants. The team received 600 submissions (up from 231 last year) and accepted less than 10% of them, according to Block.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;I think that WCUS last year really excited a lot of people, and they were interested in being a part of it,&amp;#8221; Block said. &amp;#8220;We also had quite a bit more time on the speaker applications, since in 2015 we planned the entire conference in just about three months.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;One exciting change this year is that &lt;a href=&quot;https://2016.us.wordcamp.org/2016/11/02/wordcamp-us-live-stream/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;live stream tickets&lt;/a&gt; will be free for those who are not able to attend the event. There&amp;#8217;s no limit on the number of people who can watch live.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;We really felt like there shouldn’t be a barrier to entry in attending WCUS,&amp;#8221; Block said. &amp;#8220;It’s the community’s conference, and everyone should be able to &amp;#8216;attend&amp;#8217; no matter where they physically are. We have some incredible sponsors, and making the live stream free felt like the best move.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Last year&amp;#8217;s live stream tickets included swag from the event, and WCUS 2016 will have commemorative t-shirts for sale in the swag store. In addition to the live stream, all of the sessions will be recorded and uploaded to WordPress.tv. If you are joining by live stream, make sure to &lt;a href=&quot;https://2016.us.wordcamp.org/tickets/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;reserve your ticket&lt;/a&gt; in advance. You can also &lt;a href=&quot;https://2016.us.wordcamp.org/live-stream/attendee-test/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;test your computer for compatibility&lt;/a&gt; ahead of the event.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;epoch-width-sniffer&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Mon, 07 Nov 2016 21:47:35 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Sarah Gooding&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:41;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:45:&quot;WPTavern: Take the 2016 WordPress User Survey&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:29:&quot;https://wptavern.com/?p=63524&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:56:&quot;https://wptavern.com/take-the-2016-wordpress-user-survey&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1483:&quot;&lt;p&gt;With &lt;a href=&quot;https://2016.us.wordcamp.org/&quot;&gt;WordCamp US&lt;/a&gt; a little less than a month away, it&amp;#8217;s time to take the &lt;a href=&quot;https://wordpressdotorg.polldaddy.com/s/wordpress-2016-survey&quot;&gt;2016 WordPress user survey&lt;/a&gt;. The survey is quick and easy to fill out with only a few questions to answer. Results are anonymized and will be shared at this year&amp;#8217;s State of the Word presentation.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Results from last year&amp;#8217;s survey were not shared during Matt Mullenweg&amp;#8217;s State of the Word presentation. During the &lt;a href=&quot;https://2015.us.wordcamp.org/2015/12/05/state-of-the-word-live-blog/&quot;&gt;question and answer&lt;/a&gt; portion, Mullenweg was asked about the results.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;#8220;Lots of data to go over, but basically more people are using WordPress, app development is growing, lots of people are making their living with WordPress, and other great trends are showing up,&amp;#8221; Mullenweg responded. &amp;#8220;We’ll try to do a blog post about it.&amp;#8221;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;A post highlighting the results from the 2015 survey has yet to be published.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In 2014, 33K people took the survey and of those 33K, 7,539 or 25% said they make their living from WordPress. Over 90% of respondents said they built more than one site.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you use WordPress, please take a few minutes to complete the survey. Also, &lt;a href=&quot;https://2016.us.wordcamp.org/tickets/&quot;&gt;tickets are still available&lt;/a&gt; to attend WordCamp US December 2-4.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;epoch-width-sniffer&quot;&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Mon, 07 Nov 2016 17:55:03 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Jeff Chandler&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:42;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:11:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:1:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:23:&quot;HeroPress: Finally SSL!&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:29:&quot;https://heropress.com/?p=1481&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:34:&quot;https://heropress.com/finally-ssl/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:2741:&quot;&lt;p&gt;I&amp;#8217;ve been wanting to get SSL on HeroPress for a long time, but couldn&amp;#8217;t for a variety of reasons. Well, it&amp;#8217;s finally there! That means the &lt;a href=&quot;https://heropress.com/plugin/&quot;&gt;HeroPress Widget&lt;/a&gt; will finally work properly on sites running SSL, I could someday do a Give campaign, etc.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;One downside is that it broke our connection to WordPress Planet. It&amp;#8217;s fixed now, but while it was down there were two essays that didn&amp;#8217;t make it to the News widget in WordPress, and that made a big difference.  Here they are, using WordPress&amp;#8217; cool oembed tools. Check&amp;#8217;em out and leave a comment if you&amp;#8217;re willing.&lt;/p&gt;
